Umm Walad's Status Equivalent to Mudabbar in Diyat
Concluding statement equating umm walad with mudabbar in diyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that umm walad is equivalent to mudabbar in diyat for multiple crimes, and explain the legal rationale for this equivalence.

Core Idea
Umm walad cannot be handed over as compensation, just like a mudabbar, because both statuses prevent transfer.

This passage concludes a discussion on diyat for multiple crimes committed by a slave. It establishes a key legal equivalence: the umm walad (a slave mother of her master's child) is treated exactly like a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death) in these rulings. Understanding this analogy is crucial for correctly applying diyat rules in cases involving these special categories of slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What is the ruling when an umm walad commits multiple intentional crimes? Does the master pay multiple blood moneys or surrender the slave?
2
Recognize the analogy
The author states that umm walad is in the rank of mudabbar. This means all rules previously stated for mudabbar apply equally to umm walad.
Mudabbar rules: only one payment of value for multiple crimes; the slave cannot be handed over.
3
Understand the rationale
Both tadbir (declaration of freedom upon death) and istilad (giving birth to the master's child) create a legal barrier preventing the slave from being transferred or given as compensation.
This barrier is similar to the effect of emancipation (itq), which also prevents transfer.
4
Apply the ruling
For multiple crimes by an umm walad, only one payment of her market value (qeemat) is due, and she remains with the master; she cannot be physically surrendered to the victims.
This applies even if the mudabbar is later freed — the same principle holds.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not fully equate umm walad with mudabbar; they allow her to be sold for debt or compensation in some cases. This contrast highlights the Hanafi position's protective nature.
Understanding ikhtilaf strengthens your legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمام احکام میں جو ہم نے بیان کئے ہیں ام ولد مدبر کے درجہ میں ہے اس لئے کہ ام ولد بنانا اس کے دینے مدبر کے مثل مانع ہے۔ تشریح مدبر نے اگر بہت سے جرائم کئے ہوں تو صرف ایک قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے تو اگر ایسے مدبر کو مولیٰ نے آزاد کر دیا ہو تب بھی یہی حکم ہوگا کوئی فرق نہ پڑے گا کیونکہ جس طرح اعتاق کی وجہ سے وہ دینے کے قابل نہیں رہا تدبیر کی وجہ سے بھی وہ دینے کے قابل نہیں تھا تو دونوں کا درجہ برابر ہو گیا۔ پھر جیسے مدبر کسی کو نہیں دیا جا سکتا۔ ام ولد کا بھی یہی حال ہے لہذا ان تمام مسائل میں ام ولد بھی مدبر کے درجہ میں ہے۔
In all the rulings that we have mentioned, umm walad is in the rank of mudabbar, because making a woman umm walad prevents her being given (as compensation) just like tadbir prevents. Explanation: If a mudabbar committed many crimes, only one value is obligatory. So if the master freed such a mudabbar, this same ruling applies; there is no difference, because just as due to emancipation he became not capable of being given, due to tadbir also he was not capable of being given, so both ranks became equal. Then just as a mudabbar cannot be given away, the same is the case of umm walad. Therefore in all these matters, umm walad is also in the rank of mudabbar.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a definitive statement establishing the legal equivalence of umm walad and mudabbar in the context of diyat for multiple crimes. The author explains that just as a mudabbar cannot be handed over to victims because his tadbir prevents sale or transfer, the same applies to an umm walad because her status prevents her being given as compensation. The rule that only one payment of value is due for multiple crimes applies equally to both, even if the mudabbar is later freed. The rationale is that the incapacity caused by tadbir and umm walad status is similar to the incapacity caused by emancipation (itq), which also prevents the slave from being given as compensation.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to her master's child and thus cannot be sold or given away as compensation while her child lives.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared him free upon the master's death; such a slave cannot be sold or given as compensation during the master's life.
قیمت (qeemat): The market value of the slave (or damaged part) assessed at the time of the crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Umm walad is legally equivalent to mudabbar in diyat: only one payment of value is due for multiple crimes, and she cannot be surrendered.

Mudabbar's Confession of Accidental Homicide Invalid
Ruling with proof on mudabbar's iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudabbar's confession of accidental homicide and explain the legal reasoning that prevents it from binding the master.

Core Idea
A mudabbar's confession of accidental homicide is invalid because the blood money obligation lies with the master.

In Hanafi fiqh, the liability for accidental homicide committed by a slave falls on the master, not the slave. This principle has a direct impact on the validity of a mudabbar's confession. This lesson examines a ruling from al-Hidayah that clarifies why such a confession is legally ineffective, even if the slave is later freed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The Mudabbar (a slave whose freedom is contingent upon the master's death) makes an iqrar (confession) that he committed an accidental homicide. The ruling is that this confession is invalid (batil) and does not obligate the master.
The confession is not merely nullified; it produces no legal effect whatsoever.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides the proof: 'because the obligation (mujib) of accidental homicide is upon his master, and his confession does not take effect against the master.' This is a rational legal argument (talil) based on ownership and liability.
The proof is not a Quranic verse or hadith but a legal maxim derived from the nature of liability.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase is 'mujib jinaayat al-khat'a 'ala sayyidihi' – the liability for accidental homicide is on the master. Since the master is the one who must pay blood money, the slave's confession cannot create a debt against the master without the master's consent or ratification.
This aligns with the general Hanafi rule that a slave's iqrar in matters of financial liability is ineffective against the master.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies whether the mudabbar has been freed or not after the confession. Even if the master later frees him, the confession made during slavery does not retrospectively bind the master.
This prevents a freed slave from using his former servitude to impose liability on the ex-master.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
If the master does not voluntarily pay, the victim's family cannot claim blood money from the master based solely on the mudabbar's confession. They would need separate proof (e.g., witnesses) of the homicide.
This protects the master from an unfounded claim based on the slave's word alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مدبر نے جنایت خطاء کا اقرار کیا تو اقرار سے مولیٰ پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا
وإذا أقر المدبر بجناية الخطأ لم يجز إقراره ولا يلزمه به شيء عتق أو لم يعتق لأن موجب جناية الخطأ على سيده وإقراره به لاينفذ على السيد . والله أعلم
ترجمہ اور جب مدبر نے خطاء جنایت کا اقرار کیا تو اس کا اقرار جائز نہیں ہے اور مولی پر اس کے اقرار کی وجہ سے کچھ لازم نہ ہو گا وہ آزاد کیا جا چکا ہو یا نہ کیا گیا ہو اس لئے کہ خطاء جنایت کا موجب اس کے آقا پر ہے اور ضمان کے بارے میں مدبر کا اقرار آقا پر نافذ نہ ہو گا ، واللہ اعلم .
تشریح مدبر اگر کوئی جنایت خطاء کرتا ہے تو ان کا تاوان آقا کو ادا کرنا پڑتا ہے اس لئے مدبر اگر خود کسی ایسی جنایت کا اقرار کرے تو اس کا اقرار غیر معتبر ہوگا اور اس کے اقرار کی وجہ سے آقا پر کچھ لازم نہ ہوگا وہ مدبر بدستور مدبر ہو یا اس کو اس کے آقا نے آزاد کر دیا ہو۔
If a mudabbar confesses to an accidental crime (jinaayat al-khat'a), his confession is not valid and nothing becomes obligatory upon his master due to it, whether he has been freed or not, because the liability for accidental crime is upon his master, and his confession does not take effect against the master. And Allah knows best.
Explanation: If a mudabbar commits an accidental crime, the master has to pay the compensation. Therefore if a mudabbar himself confesses to such a crime, his confession will be disregarded, and nothing will be obligatory upon the master due to his confession, whether the mudabbar remains a mudabbar or his master has freed him.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The Hidayah states that if a mudabbar makes a confession (iqrar) that he committed an accidental homicide (jinaayat al-khat'a), that confession is invalid and does not impose any liability on the master. The proof given is that the obligation (mujib) of accidental homicide falls on the master (as the slave's owner), and the mudabbar's confession cannot be binding upon the master because the master is not present and the slave's iqrar in matters of property liability does not affect the master's rights. This applies whether the mudabbar has been freed afterwards or not, because the confession was made during the period of liability. The tashreeh clarifies that the logic is that the master is the one who must pay the 'aql (blood money) for accidental killings by his slave, so the slave's self-incrimination cannot force the master to pay.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): A legal confession by a party admitting to a right or liability against himself.
جناية خطأ (jinaayat al-khat'a): Accidental crime (e.g., accidental killing) where the perpetrator is not criminally liable but must pay blood money ('aql) which is on the 'aasila (kinship group) or for a slave, on the master.
موجب (mujib): The legal cause or obligation that arises from an action; here, the obligation to pay blood money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the mudabbar is not a valid witness.
B) Because the obligation for accidental homicide falls on the master, not the slave.
C) Because the confession was made under duress.
D) Because accidental homicide does not require blood money.

Key Takeaway
A mudabbar's confession of accidental homicide is invalid and never binds the master, regardless of later manumission, because liability belongs to the master.

Ghasp of a Slave with a Cut Hand: Liability and Severance of Saraya
Two cases of ghasp of a slave with cut hand, distinguishing liability based on timing of the cut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings for ghasp of a hand-cut slave and explain why ghasp severs the saraya chain.

Core Idea
Ghasp severs causational chain like sale, transferring liability to usurper for estate's limited value.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two contrasting cases about a slave whose hand was cut. The ruling hinges on whether the cut occurred before or after the usurpation. Understanding the concept of saraya (spread of injury) and its severance by transfer of ownership is key to applying the Hanafi position correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and separate case 1 (master cuts hand, then usurper takes) from case 2 (master cuts hand while slave is already in usurper's possession).
2
Note the different liabilities
In case 1, usurper pays qeemat aqta' (value of hand-cut slave). In case 2, nothing is due from usurper.
3
Understand the concept of saraya
Saraya is the causal chain from injury to death. The ruling depends on whether this chain is 'cut' (qati') or not.
4
Apply the Qiyas with sale
The Hanafi proof is that ghasp is a cause of ownership (sabab al-mulk) like sale. Just as sale cuts saraya (buyer becomes responsible), ghasp also cuts it.
5
Conclude the reason for difference
In case 1, ghasp cuts saraya, so the death is attributed to the usurper's period. In case 2, the master's act occurred while the slave was already in usurper's hand, so the chain is not cut; the master remains responsible.

Source Text

بابُ غَصْب العَبْدِ و المُدبّر والصبي والجناية في ذالك
ترجمہ یہ باب ہے غلام اور مدبر اور بچہ کو غصب کرنے کا اور اس معاملہ میں جنایت کا
تشریح اس سے پہلے مدبر کی جنایت کا حکم بیان فرمایا گیا ہے اس باب میں مدبر سے صادر ہونے والی اور مدبر پر واقع ہونے والی جنایات کو بیان کیا جائیگا اور جو مدبر کے ساتھ لاحق ہیں ان کا بیان ہوگا لہذا فرمایا۔
اپنے غلام کا ہاتھ کاٹا پھر کسی نے اسے غصب کر لیا اور قطع کی وجہ سے غاصب کے ہاتھ میں ہلاک ہو گیا تو غاصب پر اس کے قطع کی قیمت ہے اور اگر آقا نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا اور قطع کی وجہ سے غاصب کے پاس وہ غلام مر گیا تو غاصب پر کچھ ضمان نہیں
قال ومن قطع يد عبده ثم غصبه رجل ومات في يده من القطع فعليه قيمته أقطع وإن كان المولى قطع يده في يد الغاصب فمات من ذلك فى يد الغاصب لاشيء عليه والفرق أن الغصب قاطع للسراية لأنه الملک کالبيع فيصير كأنه هلك بآفة سماوية فتجب قيمته أقطع ولم يوجد القاطع في الفصل الثاني فكانت السراية مضافة إلى البداية فصار المولى متلفا فيصير مستردا كيف وإنه استولى عليه وهو استرداد فيبرأ الغاصب عن الضمان
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے غلام کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا پھر اس کو کسی شخص نے غصب کر لیا اور وہ قطع کی وجہ سے غاصب کے قبضہ میں مر گیا تو غاصب پر اس کی اقطع کی قیمت ہے اور اگر آقا نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں اس کا ہاتھ کا نا ہو پس وہ قطع کی وجہ سے غاصب کے قبضہ میں مر گیا تو غاصب پر کچھ نہیں ہے اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ غصب سرایت کو ختم کرنے والا ہے اس لئے کہ غصب بیع کے مثل ملک کا سبب ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا گویا کہ وہ آسمانی آفت سے ہلاک ہوا ہے تو سرایت بدایت کی طرف مضاف ہو گی تو آقا متلف ہو گا پس وہ غاصب سے واپس لینے والا ہو گا کیسے نہ ہو۔ حالانکہ آقا اس پر قابض ہو چکا ہے اور قابض ہونا واپس لینا ہے پس غاصب ضمان سے بری ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح زید نے اپنے غلام کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا اور پھر اس حال میں بکر نے اس کو نصب کر لیا۔ پھر بکر (غاصب) کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے وہ مر گیا تو غاصب پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ لیکن پوری قیمت نہیں بلکہ وہ قیمت جو ہاتھ کٹا ہوا ہونے کی حالت میں اس کی قیمت ہے اور اگر غاصب کے پاس رہتے ہوئے مالک نے اس کا ہاتھ کا نا ہواور پھر غاصب ہی کے پاس زخم کی سرایت سے وہ مرگیا ہو تو غاصر پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
ان دونوں صورتوں میں فرق کیوں کیا گیا ہے؟
وجہ یہ ہے کہ جیسے بیچ سبب ملک ہے اسی طرح نصب بھی ملکیت کا سبب ہے اور سبب ملک کے آجانے سے سرایت ختم ہو جاتی ہے لہذا
Chapter on ghasp of a slave, mudabbar, and a child, and the crimes related to this.
Translation: This chapter is about usurping a slave, mudabbar, and a child, and the crime in this matter.
Explanation: Before this, the ruling of the mudabbar's crime was stated. In this chapter, the crimes emanating from a mudabbar and befalling a mudabbar will be explained, and matters connected with the mudabbar will be stated. Therefore he said:
If a man cut off the hand of his own slave, then someone usurped him (the slave), and he died from the cut in the hand of the usurper, then the usurper owes the value of the hand-cut slave. But if the master cut his hand while the slave was in the hand of the usurper, and he died from that cut in the hand of the usurper, nothing is due from the usurper.
Muhammad said: And [if] one who cut the hand of his slave, then a man usurped him and he died in his hand from the cut, then he owes the value of the hand-cut slave. And if the master cut his hand in the hand of the usurper and he died from that in the hand of the usurper, nothing is due from him. The difference is that ghasp cuts off saraya (the spread of injury causing death), because ghasp is a cause of ownership like sale. So it becomes as if he perished by a sky-borne calamity, so the value of the hand-cut slave becomes obligatory. But there is no cutter-off (of saraya) in the second case, so the saraya is attributed to the beginning (the master's act). So the master becomes the destroyer (mutlif). Then he becomes the restorer (mustaridd) – how? Even if he retained possession (upon the slave), that is a restoration. So the usurper is discharged from liability.
Explanation: Zaid cut off his slave's hand, then in that condition Bakr usurped him. Then while in Bakr's possession, he died. So the usurper owes his value, but not the full value; rather the value of a hand-cut slave. And if while in the usurper's possession the master cut his hand, and then from the wound the slave died while still in the usurper's hand, then nothing is due from the usurper.
Why is there a difference between these two cases?
The reason is that just as sale is a cause of ownership, similarly ghasp is also a cause of ownership, and when a cause of ownership comes, the saraya is cut off. Therefore...
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof from Imam Muhammad. It opens a new chapter on ghasp of a slave and related crimes. The ruling covers two scenarios: (1) the master cuts his slave's hand, then someone else usurps the slave, and the slave dies from that cut in the usurper's possession – the usurper owes the value of the slave in his hand-cut condition. (2) The master cuts the slave's hand while the slave is already in the usurper's possession, and the slave dies from that cut there – the usurper owes nothing. The key proof is the difference (al-farq): ghasp is a cause of ownership (sabab al-mulk) similar to sale. When ownership transfers to the usurper via ghasp, the saraya (the chain of causation from the original injury to death) is severed, and the death is treated as if from a celestial calamity – thus the usurper is liable for the value at the time of taking. In the second case, the saraya is not cut because the master's cutting occurred while the slave was already in the usurper's hand (and the ghasp had already taken place, but the ownership transfer does not cut the saraya retroactively? Actually, the explanation says there is no qati' (severance) in the second case because the master's act occurred after the ghasp, so the saraya is attributed to the master's initial act, making the master the direct destroyer. The master then is considered to have taken the slave back (istirdad) from the usurper, so the usurper is free from liability. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that ghasp transfers liability for injuries that occur after the ghasp, but pre-existing injuries continue to be the responsibility of the original owner if the death is directly caused by them after the transfer.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Wrongful usurpation or seizure of another's property without consent; it transfers the liability for damages during the period of usurpation.
سرایت (saraya): The spread of an injury (e.g., from a wound) leading to death; in diyat, the causation chain that determines who pays blood money.
قیمت اقطع (qeemat aqta'): The market value of a slave with a missing or cut-off hand (i.e., in the condition at the time of ghasp).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first case (master cuts hand, then usurper takes slave, slave dies from cut), what must the usurper pay?
A) The full value of the slave without the cut.
B) The value of the slave as a hand-cut slave (qeemat aqta').
C) Nothing, because the master caused the injury.
D) The blood money for the hand.

Key Takeaway
Ghasp cuts the causal chain of injury (saraya) like sale, making the usurper liable only for the property's value at the time of usurpation.

Liability When Mudabbar Commits Two Crimes With Different Possessors
Ruling on mudabbar who commits two crimes under different possessors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mudabbar commits two crimes under different possessors and explain the reasoning that limits liability to the slave's value divided equally.

Core Idea
A mudabbar's value is capped at one slave's price, split equally between victims, because tadbir blocks surrender without permitting ransom.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced case: a mudabbar slave commits a crime while usurped, then after return to the master commits another crime. How is liability determined? The Hanafi ruling limits the master's payment to the slave's market value, divided equally between the two sets of victims' heirs. The reasoning (talil) hinges on the master's previous tadbir creating an incapacity to surrender the slave, while the master did not choose to ransom him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The act: a mudabbar commits two crimes under two different possessors (first with the usurper, then with the master). Parties: the master (mawla), the usurper (ghasib), and the victims' heirs (awliya' al-jinaya).
2
State the ruling
The master must pay the mudabbar's market value (qimah) as a slave, divided equally between the two sets of victims' heirs.
The master does not have the option to surrender the slave or pay ransom (fida').
3
Trace the talil (legal reasoning)
The master's earlier tadbir made him unable to hand over the slave (a'jaza nafsahu 'an al-daf'), yet he did not choose ransom (lam yasir mukhtaran li-l-fida'). Thus he becomes an invalidator of the victims' rights (mubtil li-haqq awliya' al-jinaya). Since there is only one slave (ruqbah wahida), the liability cannot exceed its value.
The reasoning is based on the master's own act creating the impediment.
4
Derive the practical consequence
Both crimes give an equal claim to the slave's value because the cause (wujub) is equal for both. The value is split half and half.
No preference for the earlier or later crime.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن غصب مديرا فجنى عنده جناية ثم رده على المولى فجنى عنده جناية أخرى فعلى المولى قيمته بينهما نصفان لأن المولى بالتدبير السابق أعجز نفسه عن الدفع من غير أن يصير مختارا للفداء فيصير مبطلا حق أولياء الجناية إذ حقهم فيه ولم يمنع إلا رقبة واحدة فلا يزاد على قيمتها وتكون بين وليى الجنايتين نصفين لاستوائهما في الموجب
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے غصب کیا مد ترکو پس اس نے جنایت کی غاصب کے پاس کوئی جنایت پھر مولی کو واپس کر دیا ہو پس اس نے جنایت کی مولی کے پاس دوسری جنایت پس مولیٰ پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہو گی جو ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہو گی۔ اس لئے کہ مولیٰ نے تدبیر سابق کی وجہ سے اپنے آپ کو مد بر دینے سے عاجز کر دیا ہے۔ بغیر اس کے کہ وہ فدیہ اختیار کرنے والا ہو تو آقا اولیاء جنایت کا حق باطل کرنے والا ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ ان کا حق دینے میں ہے اور آقا نے صرف ایک رقبہ کو روکا ہے۔ پس ایک رقبہ کی قیمت سے بڑھایا نہیں جائے گا۔ اور قیمت دونوں والی جنایت کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہو گی ان دونوں کے مستوی ہونے کی وجہ سے
He said: And whoever usurps a mudabbar, and he commits a crime with him (the usurper), then he returns him to the master, and he commits another crime with the master, then upon the master is his value, divided equally between them (the two sets of heirs), because the master, by the previous tadbir, has rendered himself unable to hand over (the slave) without becoming free to ransom (just yet), so he becomes invalidator of the right of the crime's heirs. For their right is in him (the slave), and the master only prevented one neck (one slave), so the value will not be exceeded, and it will be between the two heirs equally because of the equal cause.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This ruling deals with a mudabbar slave (one promised emancipation upon the master's death). If someone usurps this mudabbar, and the mudabbar commits a crime (like murder or causing bodily harm) while with the usurper, then the usurper returns the mudabbar to the master, and the mudabbar commits another crime while with the master, the master is liable to pay the value of the mudabbar, but this value is divided equally between the two sets of victims' heirs. The reasoning: The master, by declaring tadbir earlier, has incapacitated himself from surrendering the slave to the crime victims (because a mudabbar cannot be sold or given away for a crime; he must remain with the master until death, at which point he goes free). However, the master did not choose to ransom the slave (pay the blood money himself) — he is not given that option because the slave is not a simple slave. So the master holds onto the mudabbar, thereby obstructing the victims' rights. Since there is only one slave (only one 'neck' — ruqbah), the total liability cannot exceed his value at the time (the full value, not the value as a mudabbar?). That full value is then split between the two sets of heirs, as both crimes have equal claim to the slave's value. The commentarial explanation adds that because the mudabbar cannot be surrendered, the master becomes a 'mubtil' (invalidator) of the victims' rights, so he must pay the value.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised emancipation upon the master's death (tadbir). This status prevents the master from selling or gifting the slave, but the slave remains in the master's possession.
فداء (fida'): Ransom; the option for the master to pay blood money (diyah) to keep the slave alive after the slave commits a crime. This option is not available for a mudabbar in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the liability for the mudabbar's two crimes limited to his value and divided equally?
A) Because the master is not responsible for crimes committed by a mudabbar.
B) Because the master, by declaring tadbir, is unable to hand over the slave and did not choose ransom, so he holds one slave; the value cannot exceed the price of that one slave, and both victims have equal right in it.
C) Because the mudabbar is worth more than a regular slave.
D) Because the crimes were both accidental.

Key Takeaway
The master pays the mudabbar's value divided equally because tadbir prevents surrender without enabling ransom, and the single slave cannot satisfy two full claims.

Mudabbar's Crimes: Imam Muhammad vs. Shaykhayn on Compensation
Explaining dispute between Imam Muhammad and Shaykhayn on mudabbar compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn regarding the mudabbar's compensation and apply the consensus ruling for the second scenario.

Core Idea
When a mudabbar is usurped and commits a second crime, the master's recovery from the usurper may or may not be passed to the first victim.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for a mudabbar slave who commits crimes with both the master and a usurper. The core question is whether the master keeps the half-value recovered from the usurper or must give it to the first victim. By working through the proofs of Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn, you will understand the legal reasoning behind each position and the consensus ruling in a specific variant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The mudabbar commits a first crime at the master's, then is usurped and commits a second crime. The master is liable for the full value, split half-half between victims.
The slave is a mudabbar (to be freed on master's death).
2
State the Dispute
Imam Muhammad holds the master keeps the recovered half from the usurper; the Shaykhayn say the master gives it to the first victim and then recovers again.
Both positions are within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Muhammad argues that the recovery is compensation for what the master paid, so giving it again would double the first victim's claim. The Shaykhayn argue the first victim originally deserved the full value and the half is found free, so he completes his right.
The reasoning is aqli (rational), based on preventing double recovery vs. completing the first right.
4
Apply the Second Scenario (Consensus)
When the first crime occurs at the master's and the second at the usurper's, consensus (bil-ijma') says the master gives the recovered half to the first victim and does not recover from the usurper again.
This is because the right to that half is established by the second crime in the usurper's hand.

قال وإن كان جنى عند المولى فغصبه رجل فجنى عنده جناية أخرى فعلى المولى قيمته بينهما نصفان ويرجع بنصف القيمة على الغاصب لما بينا فى الفصل الأول غير أن استحقاق النصف حصل بالجناية الثانية إذ كانت هى فى يد الغاصب فيدفعه إلى ولى الجناية الأولى ولا يرجع به على الغاصب وهذا بالإجماع ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور اگر آقا کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اس کو کسی شخص نے غصب کر لیا پس غاصب کے پاس دوسری جنایت کی پس مولی پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے، جو ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہو گی ۔ اور آقا نصف قیمت کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم پہلی صورت میں بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ علاوہ اس بات کے کہ نصف استحقاق دوسری جنایت کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ دوسری جنایت غاصب کے قبضہ میں ہوئی ہے پس آقا اس نصف کو ولی جنایت اولی کو دیدے گا اور اس کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع نہیں کرے گا اور یہ بالا جماع ہے۔
Near is that Muhammad said: The master will recover half the value of the mudabbar, so that half remains for the master. Commentary: I have explained this before. Imam Muhammad's proof: Because what the master recovers from the usurper is compensation for what he paid to the first victim's kin, so he does not pay it to him, lest it lead to the combination of compensation and the compensated in the ownership of one person, and lest the entitlement be repeated. Translation: The amount the master recovers from the usurper is the compensation for what he gave to the first victim's kin, so the master does not give that half to the first victim's kin, to avoid the combination of compensation and the compensated in the ownership of one person, and to avoid repeated entitlement. Explanation: This is Imam Muhammad's proof. The Shaykhayn's proof: They said that the first (victim's kin) has the right to the entire value because when the mudabbar committed the crime in his favor, no one contested him, and his right was only reduced due to the contest of the second. So when he finds something from the slave's compensation in the master's hand free (of other claims), he takes it to complete his right. When he takes it from him, the master recovers from the usurper what he took, because it was taken from his hand due to a cause that occurred in the usurper's hand. Translation: And the Shaykhayn's proof: The first has the right to the full value because when the mudabbar committed the crime in his right, no one contested him, and the first's right was reduced only due to the contest of the second. So when he (the first) finds something from the slave's compensation in the master's possession free of other claims, the first takes it to complete his right. When the first takes it from him, the master recovers from the usurper the amount he took, because that amount was taken from his hand due to a cause that occurred in the usurper's hand. Explanation: This is the Shaykhayn's proof. So when the first victim's kin took that half from the master, the master will again take half from the usurper and this half remains with the master. Why? Because this half which the first victim's kin took from the master is in return for the crime that occurred while the mudabbar was in the usurper's possession, so the master has the right to take it again. Then: If the crime occurred at the master's, then someone usurped him (the slave), then he committed another crime at the usurper's, then the master owes his value between them half and half, and he recovers half the value from the usurper, as we explained in the first chapter, except that the entitlement to that half is established by the second crime because it occurred in the usurper's hand, so he pays it to the first victim's kin and does not recover it from the usurper. This is by consensus. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: And if he committed a crime at the master's, then someone usurped him, then he committed another crime at the usurper's, then the master owes his value, which is half-half between them. And the master recovers half the value from the usurper due to the same proof we mentioned in the first case, except that the entitlement to half is established by the second crime because it occurred in the usurper's hand, so the master gives that half to the first victim's kin and does not recover it from the usurper, and this is by consensus.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) within the chapter of Diat regarding a mudabbar (slave who will be freed upon master's death) who commits crimes at different times. The scenario: the mudabbar commits a first crime while with the master, then is usurped by a ghasib (usurper), and while in the usurper's possession commits a second crime. The master is liable for the value (qimah) of the mudabbar, which is divided equally between the two victims' kin (awliya' al-jinaya). The master then recovers half the value from the usurper. The dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that the master keeps the recovered half for himself, because it is compensation for what he already paid to the first victim. Giving it to the first victim would result in double compensation (badal and mubadal) in one person's ownership. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the first victim originally deserved the full value, but his right was reduced due to the second victim's claim. Therefore, when the master recovers any amount from the usurper, that amount should go to the first victim to complete his right. Then the master can again recover that amount from the usurper, as it was taken due to a cause that occurred in the usurper's possession. The text then presents a second scenario: if the first crime occurred at the master's, then the slave was usurped and committed the second crime at the usurper's, then it is by consensus (bil-ijma') that the master gives the recovered half to the first victim and does not recover it from the usurper again. This is because the right to that half is established due to the second crime, which occurred in the usurper's hand. Thus, the master pays it to the first victim and has no further recourse against the usurper.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who will become free upon the master's death (tadbir).
غاصب (ghasib): One who unlawfully takes property (here, the slave) without right.
ولی جنایت (wali al-jinaya): The victim's heir or legal representative entitled to blood money (diyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the mudabbar scenario where the first crime occurs at the master's and the second at the usurper's, what is the consensus (ijma') ruling regarding the half recovered from the usurper?
A) The master keeps it and recovers again.
B) The master gives it to the first victim and does not recover it again.
C) The master gives it to the second victim.
D) The master returns it to the usurper.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the mudabbar's compensation hinges on whether to prioritize avoiding double recovery (Muhammad) or completing the first victim's original right (Shaykhayn).

Extending Mudabbar Compensation Rulings to a Regular Slave
Extending mudabbar ruling to regular slave via qiyas with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation rules for a regular slave (abd) in diyat cases and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the master's recourse against the usurper.

Core Idea
A regular slave follows the same diyat compensation pattern as a mudabbar, differing only in payment form: slave vs. value.

This passage extends the compensation rulings previously established for a mudabbar (a slave with tadbir) to a regular slave (abd). The key difference is that the master hands over the slave itself (since it can be sold) rather than its value. Alongside this qiyas, an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf appears regarding whether the master can recover the same half-value from the usurper twice in one scenario. Let us examine the two scenarios and the scholars' positions.

Guided Path
1
Recall the mudabbar compensation pattern
From the previous passage, the mudabbar ruling dictates that when a mudabbar commits crimes partly in the usurper's possession, the master pays the victims with the mudabbar's value, then recovers half from the usurper and either gives it to the first victim (Shaykhayn) or keeps it (Muhammad).
This pattern is the 'asl' (original case) in the qiyas.
2
Identify the two scenarios for the regular slave
Scenario 1: the slave commits a crime at the usurper's, is returned, and then commits a second crime at the master's. Scenario 2: the slave commits a first crime at the master's, is then usurped, and commits a second crime at the usurper's.
The text describes both orders of events.
3
Apply qiyas to determine the ruling
The underlying reasoning (illa) – the usurper's possession causing the first crime and the master's liability – is identical. Hence, the same compensation scheme applies, except the master delivers the slave (the far') instead of its value (as in the asl).
The qiyas is jaliy (clear) because the illa is obvious.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf in Scenario 1
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that after handing over the slave to both victims, the master recovers half the value from the usurper, gives it to the first victim's kin, and then recovers that same half again from the usurper. Muhammad says the master recovers half and keeps it (i.e., does not pay the first victim a second time).
The ikhtilaf concerns whether the usurper is liable twice for the same half.
5
Distinguish the slave ruling from the mudabbar ruling
The only difference is the form of payment: for a regular slave, the master hands over the slave (which can be sold or divided); for a mudabbar, he hands over the value (since the mudabbar cannot be sold before the master's death).
This distinction is explicitly stated in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام نے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی غاصب نے واپس کر دیا پھر مولی کے پاس دوسری جنایت کی تو حکم اثم وضع المسألة فى العبد فقال ومن غصب عبدا فجنى فى يده ثم رده فجنى جناية أخرى فإن المولى يدفعه إلى ولى الجنايتين ثم يرجع على الغاصب بنصف القيمة فيدفعه إلى الأول ويرجع به على الغاصب وهذا عند أبى حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد يرجع بنصف القيمة فيسلم له وإن جنى عند المولى ثم غصبه فجنى في يده دفعه المولى نصفين ويرجع بنصف قيمته فيدفعه إلى الأول ولا يرجع به والجواب فى العبد كالجواب في المدير في جميع ما ذكرنا إلا أن في هذا الفصل يدفع المولى العبد وفي الأول يدفع القيمة
A slave committed a crime at the usurper's, the usurper returned him, then he committed another crime at the master's. Then the ruling: Then he placed the issue regarding the slave. He said: Whoever usurps a slave, and the slave commits a crime in his hand, then he returns him, and the slave commits another crime (at the master's), then the master hands the slave over to the two victims' kin, then he recovers half the value from the usurper, gives it to the first (victim's kin), and recovers it again from the usurper. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: he recovers half the value and it is given to him (i.e., he keeps it). And if the slave committed a crime at the master's, then he (the slave) was usurped, and committed a crime in his (the usurper's) hand, then the master hands over the slave (divided) half-half, and recovers half its value, gives it to the first, and does not recover it again. And the answer for the slave is like the answer for the mudabbar in all that we have mentioned, except that in this chapter the master hands over the slave, while in the first (mudabbar) he hands over the value.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage applies the same rulings to a regular slave (ghulam) as were established for the mudabbar. It presents two scenarios: (1) If the slave commits a crime while with the usurper, then is returned and commits another crime at the master's, then the master hands over the slave to both victims' kin. The master recovers half the value from the usurper, gives it to the first victim, and recovers it again from the usurper. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad differs, holding that the master keeps the recovered half. (2) If the slave commits the first crime at the master's, then is usurped and commits a second crime at the usurper's, then the master hands over the slave half-half (i.e., the slave is divided between the victims), recovers half its value from the usurper, gives it to the first victim, and does not recover it from the usurper again. The text concludes that the ruling for the slave is identical to that for the mudabbar, except that in the case of the slave, the master hands over the slave itself (since the slave can be sold to satisfy claims), whereas in the case of the mudabbar, the master hands over the value (because the mudabbar is prepatory and cannot be sold).

Key Terms
عبد (abd): A regular slave (not mudabbar).
قیمة (qimah): Market value of the slave, used as compensation.

C) For the mudabbar, the master hands over the slave itself.
D) There is no difference.

Key Takeaway
The compensation pattern for a regular slave (abd) in diyat cases is identical to that of a mudabbar, with the sole difference being that the master delivers the slave (which can be sold) instead of its value; the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the master's recourse remains the same.

Slave's Two Jinayat at Master and Usurper: Liability and Recourse
Imam Muhammad's ruling on liability when a slave commits jinayat at master and usurper

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a slave commits two jinayat at different possessors and explain the master's obligation and flow of compensation.

Core Idea
The master owes full value for both jinayat, but recovery from the usurper is only half, which must go to the first victim.

When a slave commits jinaayah while in the master's possession, then is usurped and commits another jinaayah, the master remains liable for both. But the usurper's liability for the second jinaayah changes the recovery pattern. This lesson unpacks Imam Muhammad's ruling, showing how the master's payment is divided and why a recovered half must be forwarded to the first victim, not kept. The ruling is a consensus among early Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two jinayat and their locations
Determine the sequence: the first jinaayah occurs at the master's, the second at the usurper's after ghasb. Each jinaayah creates a separate diyat claim.
The location matters because it affects who ultimately bears the cost of each jinaayah.
2
Determine the master's total liability
The master owes the full value of the slave (or the diyat equivalent) to the two victims, divided equally – half for each jinaayah. This is a wajib obligation.
The master's liability is not reduced by the occurrence of the second jinaayah at the usurper's.
3
Analyze the master's right of recourse against the usurper
The master recovers half the value from the usurper, because the second jinaayah happened while the slave was in the usurper's hand. This half corresponds to the second jinaayah's share.
The usurper is directly liable for the half incurred during his possession.
4
Understand why the recovered half goes to the first victim
The recovered half must be given to the first victim, not the second. Reason: the second victim's claim is directly against the half incurred at the usurper's; the master's recovery from the usurper reimburses him for paying that half, but he must then discharge the first victim's claim with that same half.
This avoids double liability: the master pays the first victim from the recovered amount, not from his own pocket again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صادر ہوئی تھی اس لئے آقا دوبارہ لینے کا حق دار ہوگا۔
آقا کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اس کو کسی نے غصب کر لیا پھر غاصب کے پاس دوسری جنایت کی مولیٰ پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے جو ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہوگی اور آقا نصف قیمت سے غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا
قال وإن كان جنى عند المولى فغصبه رجل فجنى عنده جناية أخرى فعلى المولى قيمته بينهما نصفان ويرجع بنصف القيمة على الغاصب لما بينا فى الفصل الأول غير أن استحقاق النصف حصل بالجناية الثانية إذ كانت هى فى يد الغاصب فيدفعه إلى ولى الجناية الأولى ولا يرجع به على الغاصب وهذا بالإجماع ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور اگر آقا کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اس کو کسی شخص نے غصب کر لیا پس غاصب کے پاس دوسری جنایت کی پس مولی پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے، جو ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہو گی ۔ اور آقا نصف قیمت کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم پہلی صورت میں بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ علاوہ اس بات کے کہ نصف استحقاق دوسری جنایت کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ دوسری جنایت غاصب کے قبضہ میں ہوئی ہے پس آقا اس نصف کو ولی جنایت اولی کو دیدے گا اور اس کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع نہیں کرے گا اور یہ بالا جماع ہے۔ تشریح اس کی تفسیر ظاہر ہے اس میں اور اول میں یہ فرق ہے کہ اول میں دوسری جنایت آقا کے پاس ہوتی ہے۔ اور ثانی غاصب کے پاس اور اس میں بالکل اس کا عکس ہے یعنی پہلی مالک کے پاس اور دوسری غاصب کے پاس ہے۔
اور دوسرا فرق یہ ہے کہ جب آقا نے غاصب سے نصف قیمت وصول کی تو اس کو ولی جنایت اولی ملے گا تو اب اس نصف کو آقا غاصب سے دوبارہ لینے کا حق دار نہ ہوگا اور یہاں اس نصف ماخوذ کا ولی جنایت اولی کو دینا بالا جماع ہے۔ یعنی یہاں امام محمد کا شیخین سے اختلاف نہیں ہے۔
It had been issued, therefore the master will be entitled to take it again. He committed jinaayah at the master's, then someone usurped him, then he committed another jinaayah at the usurper's; the master owes his value, which is half-and-half between the two (victims), and the master will recover half the value from the usurper. He (Imam Muhammad) said: And if he committed jinaayah at the master's, then a man usurped him, then he committed another jinaayah at his (the usurper's), then the master owes his value between them half-and-half, and he recovers half the value from the usurper, as we explained in the first section, except that the entitlement to the half occurred due to the second jinaayah since it was in the usurper's hand, so he gives it to the wali of the first jinaayah and does not recover it from the usurper, and this is by consensus. And the master will recover half the value from the usurper because of the proof we stated in the first case. Except that the entitlement to the half occurred due to the second jinaayah because the second jinaayah occurred in the usurper's possession; so the master will give that half to the wali of the first jinaayah and will not recover it from the usurper, and this is by consensus. Explanation: Its explanation is clear. The difference between this and the first case is that in the first, the second jinaayah occurred at the master's, and in the second, at the usurper's, and this is the exact opposite, i.e., the first is at the owner's and the second at the usurper's. And the second difference is that when the master receives half the value from the usurper, he will give it to the wali of the first jinaayah; then he is not entitled to take that half again from the usurper, and giving that collected half to the wali of the first jinaayah is by consensus, i.e., there is no difference between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs here.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam Muhammad regarding a slave who commits two separate jinaayat (offenses requiring diyat) while in different hands. The slave first commits a jinaayah while in the possession of his master (mawla), then is usurped (ghasb) by someone, and commits a second jinaayah while in the usurper's possession. The ruling states that the master owes the full value of the slave (his diyat value) to the two victims, divided equally between them—half for the victim of the first jinaayah and half for the victim of the second. However, because the second jinaayah occurred while the slave was in the usurper's hand, the master recovers half the value from the usurper (the half corresponding to the second jinaayah). But crucially, the master must give that recovered half to the victim of the first jinaayah, not to the second victim. The reason is that the second jinaayah's victim has a direct claim on the half incurred in the usurper's hand; the master's recovery from the usurper is to reimburse him for paying that half, but he must forward it to the first victim because the first victim's claim is against the master directly. The passage emphasizes that this ruling is by consensus (ijma') among the early Hanafi imams—there is no ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on this specific point. The commentary (tashrih) clarifies the difference from a previous case (mentioned earlier in the text) where the second jinaayah occurred at the master's, leading to a different recovery pattern. Here, the reversal of locations (first at master, second at usurper) changes the flow of recovery.

Key Terms
جناية (jinaayah): A criminal offense (like homicide or wounding) that requires diyat (blood money) or qisas.
غصب (ghasb): Unlawful usurpation of property, taking possession of something without the owner's consent.
ولي الجناية (wali al-jinaayah): The victim or the legal guardian of the victim entitled to claim diyat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To the victim of the second jinaayah
B) To the victim of the first jinaayah
C) He keeps it for himself
D) He gives half to each victim

Key Takeaway
When a slave commits jinayat at different possessors, the master's full liability remains, but recovery from the usurper relates only to the second jinaayah, and that recovery must be applied to the first victim.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Slave Jinayat: First at Usurper, Then Returned, Second at Master
Imam Muhammad presents a case and the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the master's obligations when a slave commits two jinaayat (first at usurper's, then at master's after return) and explain the practical difference between the two views.

Core Idea
When a slave commits jinaayah at usurper and later at master, the two shaykhs make the usurper pay twice; Muhammad lets the master keep the recovery.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a multi-step jinaayah scenario. A slave commits the first jinaayah while possessed by a usurper, is returned, then commits a second jinaayah at the master's. The key question: who bears the financial burden of the first jinaayah? The answer depends on whether we follow the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf or the view of Imam Muhammad. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to analyze multi-party liability in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
A slave commits a jinaayah while being possessed by a usurper (ghasib). The usurper returns him to the master. Then the slave commits another jinaayah while with the master. Two jinaayat, two victims.
Note that the slave becomes subject to claims from both victims.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
The master must hand over the slave to both victims jointly. Then the master recovers half the slave's value from the usurper (representing the liability for the first jinaayah), gives that half to the first victim, and then recovers that same half again from the usurper. The usurper bears the ultimate cost of the first jinaayah.
The master does not bear the loss; he recovers from the usurper and passes it to the first victim, then recovers again.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that the master recovers half the value from the usurper and keeps it for himself (yaslam lahu). The first victim's claim is against the slave or its value, not against the master personally. The master does not have to give the recovered half to the first victim.
Under Muhammad's view, the usurper's liability is limited to the loss of value; the first victim must seek his diyat from the slave's value directly.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the majority view, the master must actively transfer the recovered amount to the first victim and then reclaim from the usurper. Under Muhammad's view, the master keeps it, and the first victim must pursue the slave or its value separately.
This changes the flow of money and the ultimate burden of the jinaayah.
5
Contrast with the mudabbir and the reverse scenario
The same dispute applies to a regular slave as to a mudabbir, with the only difference being that for a regular slave the master hands over the slave itself, while for a mudabbir he hands over its value. Also, the passage mentions the reverse case (first at master, then at usurper) with a slight variation in the master's recovery.
Understanding the analogical reasoning helps apply the rule consistently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام نے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی غاصب نے واپس کر دیا پھر مولی کے پاس دوسری جنایت کی تو حکم
اثم وضع المسألة فى العبد فقال ومن غصب عبدا فجنى فى يده ثم رده فجنى جناية أخرى فإن المولى يدفعه إلى ولى الجنايتين ثم يرجع على الغاصب بنصف القيمة فيدفعه إلى الأول ويرجع به على الغاصب وهذا عند أبى حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد يرجع بنصف القيمة فيسلم له وإن جنى عند المولى ثم غصبه فجنى في يده دفعه المولى نصفين ويرجع بنصف قيمته فيدفعه إلى الأول ولا يرجع به والجواب فى العبد كالجواب في المدير في جميع ما ذكرنا إلا أن في هذا الفصل يدفع المولى العبد وفي الأول يدفع القيمة
ترجمہ پھر محمد نے مسئلہ کو غلام کے بارے میں وضع کیا پس فرمایا اور جس نے غصب کیا غلام کو پس اس نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں جنایت کی پھر غاصب نے اس کو واپس کر دیا پس اس نے دوسری جنایت کی پس مولی اس کو دونوں ولی جنایت کو دیدے گا پھر غاصب سے اس کی نصف قیمت واپس لے گا پس اس کو اول کی جانب دیدے گا اور اس کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا اور یہ تیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور محمد نے فرمایا کہ نصف قیمت کے بارے میں رجوع کرے گا پس وہ آقا کے لئے محفوظ رہے گی ۔ اور اگر اس نے آقا کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اس کو غصب کیا ہو پس اس کے قبضہ میں اس نے جنایت کی تو آقا غلام کو آدھا آدھا دیدے گا اور آقا اس کی نصف قیمت کے بارے میں رجوع کرے گا ( غاصب پر ) پس اس کو اوّل کو دیدگا اور اس کے بارے میں رجوع نہیں کرے گا اور جواب غلام کے بارے میں مدبر کے جواب کے مثل ہے ان تمام صورتوں میں جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہیں مگر اس صورت میں آقا غلام کو دے گا اور پہلی میں قیمت کو ۔ تشریح اس ساری تفصیل کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر بجائے مدبر کے غلام ہو تو تب بھی یہی تفصیل اور اختلاف ہے لیکن اتنا فرق ہے کہ غلام کی صورت میں غلام دینا پڑتا ہے اور مدبر کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت اور باقی صورت وہی ہے جو پہلے مسئلہ کی تھی لیکن امام محمد نے مد بر کا بیان کر کے پھر اس کو بھی بیان فرمایا ہے اس لئے امام محمد کے طرز کے مطابق مصنف نے یہی طریقہ اختیار فرمایا ہے۔
The slave committed jinaayah at the usurper's, the usurper returned him, then he committed another jinaayah at the master's; what is the ruling? Then he placed the mas'alah regarding the slave and said: Whoever usurps a slave and he commits jinaayah in his hand, then he returns him and he commits another jinaayah, then the master hands him over to the wali of both jinaayat, then he recovers half the value from the usurper, then gives it to the first (wali) and recovers it back from the usurper. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: He recovers half the value and it stays safe for him. And if he committed jinaayah at the master's, then he usurped him and he committed jinaayah in his hand, the master gives him half-and-half and recovers half his value (from the usurper), then gives it to the first and does not recover it. And the answer for the slave is like the answer for the mudabbir in all we have mentioned, except that in this chapter the master gives the slave, while in the first he gives the value. Translation: Then Muhammad placed the mas'alah regarding the slave and said: Whoever usurps a slave and he commits jinaayah in the usurper's possession, then the usurper returns him, then he commits another jinaayah, then the master gives him to the wali of both jinaayat, then he takes back half his value from the usurper, then gives it to the first (wali) and will recover it from the usurper. This is according to the two shaykhs. And Muhammad said: He recovers half the value, then it remains safe for the master. And if he committed jinaayah at the master's, then he usurped him and he committed jinaayah in his hand, then the master gives him half-and-half and recovers half his value (from the usurper), then gives it to the first and does not recover it. And the answer for the slave is like the answer for the mudabbir in all these cases we have mentioned, except that in this case the master gives the slave, while in the first he gives the value. Explanation: The summary of all this detail is that if instead of a mudabbir there is a slave, then also this same detail and ikhtilaf applies, but there is this difference that in the case of a slave the slave must be given, and in the case of a mudabbir its value; and the rest of the situation is the same as the previous mas'alah. But Imam Muhammad after mentioning the mudabbir also mentioned this, so according to Imam Muhammad's style the author adopted this method.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a scenario where a slave commits two jinaayat: the first while in the possession of a usurper (ghasib), then the usurper returns the slave to the master, and the slave commits a second jinaayah while back in the master's possession. The passage first states the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs): the master must hand over the slave himself to the victims of both jinaayat (i.e., the slave becomes subject to qisas or diyat claim), then the master recovers half the value of the slave from the usurper (the half corresponding to the first jinaayah), gives that half to the victim of the first jinaayah, and then the master can again recover that same half from the usurper (meaning the usurper is ultimately liable for the first jinaayah's diyat). The wording 'يرجع به على الغاصب' indicates the master recovers it back from the usurper. Imam Muhammad's position differs: he says the master recovers half the value from the usurper and it stays safe for him (يسلم له), meaning the master does not have to give that half to the first victim; rather, the master keeps it as compensation for the loss of the slave's value due to the first jinaayah. The first victim's claim lies directly against the slave (or his value) but not against the master personally? The passage also mentions the opposite case (first at master, second at usurper) as a comparison, and notes that the ruling for a regular slave is analogous to that for a mudabbir (a slave promised emancipation upon master's death) in all details, except that for a regular slave the master hands over the slave himself, while for a mudabbir he hands over its value (since a mudabbir cannot be sold). The commentary (tashrih) summarizes that the same detail and ikhtilaf applies to a slave as to a mudabbir, with the noted difference in what is handed over.

Key Terms
مولی (mawla): Master or owner of the slave.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave who has been promised emancipation upon the master's death, a type of 'contract' (tadbir).
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs, i.e., Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He gives it to the victim of the first jinaayah
B) He gives it to the victim of the second jinaayah
C) He keeps it for himself
D) He divides it between both victims

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute over slave jinaayat, the majority view holds the usurper ultimately liable for the first jinaayah, while Imam Muhammad places that burden on the master.

Liability of the Master for a Mudabbir's Multiple Jinayat at the Usurper's
Imam Muhammad rules on a mudabbir's two jinayat at the usurper's

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mudabbir commits two jinaayat at the usurper's with an intervening return, and explain the master's liability and right of recovery.

Core Idea
Master pays one value divided between victims, then recovers full value from the usurper.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's ruling addresses a scenario where a mudabbir is usurped, commits jinaayah, is returned to the master, then usurped again and commits a second jinaayah. The key question is: who bears the diyat? The ruling clarifies that the master pays the slave's value (since the mudabbir cannot be handed over due to tadbir) and then recovers the full amount from the usurper. Let's walk through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of events
The scenario has four phases: (1) usurpation of mudabbir, (2) first jinaayah at usurper's, (3) return to master, (4) second usurpation, (5) second jinaayah at usurper's. Understand this timeline to apply the ruling correctly.
The two jinaayat occur at different possession periods (both at usurper's), but with a return in between.
2
Determine the master's primary liability
Because the mudabbir's raqabah is restricted by tadbir, the master cannot surrender the slave to the victims. Instead, he must pay the mudabbir's full value as diyat. The text states: 'because he restricted a single body by tadbir, so one value is obligatory'.
This is a single value, not two separate values.
3
Apportion the value between the two victims
The value is divided equally (half-and-half) between the victims of the two jinaayat. Since both jinaayat occurred while the mudabbir was in the usurper's possession, they share the same liability source.
The master pays one value but splits it between the two victims.
4
Understand the master's right of recourse
After paying the value, the master recovers the full amount from the usurper. The justification is that both jinaayat happened while the mudabbir was in the usurper's hand; hence the usurper is ultimately responsible.
The master does not absorb any loss; the usurper bears the full diyat.
5
Confirm the intra-Hanafi agreement
The commentary notes that Imām Muhammad's ruling is agreed upon (ittifāq) by the Ṣāḥibayn. There is no dispute within the Hanafi school on this point.
This strengthens the reliability of the fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے مدبر کو غصب کیا مدبر نے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اسے مولیٰ کی طرف لوٹا دیا پھر اسے غصب کیا پھر دوسری جنایت غاصب کے پاس کی مولیٰ پر اس کی قیمت ہے جو دونوں کے درمیان نصف نصف ہوگی
قال ومين غصب مدبرا فجنى عنده جناية ثم رده على المولى ثم غصبه ثم جنى عنده جناية فعلى المولى قیمته بينهما نصفان لأنه منع رقبة واحدة بالتدبير فتجب عليه قيمة واحدة ثم يرجع بقيمته على الغاصب لأن الجنايتين كانتا في يد الغاصب
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے مدبر کو نصب کیا پس اس نے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اس کو مولی کو واپس کر دیا پھر اس کو غصب کیا پھر اس کے پاس جنایت کی تو مولیٰ پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے جو ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہو گی اس لئے کہ آقا نے تدبیر کی وجہ سے ایک رقبہ کو روکا ہے تو اس پر ایک قیمت واجب ہے پھر آقا اس کی پوری قیمت کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا اس لئے کہ دونوں جنایتین غاصب کے قبضہ میں ہوئی ہیں ۔ تشریح اگر غاصب نے مدبر غصب کیا اور مدبر نے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی اور غاصب نے سید بر آقا کو واپس کر دیا اور پھر دوبارہ غصب کر لیا اور مدبر نے غاصب کے پاس دوبارہ پھر جنایت کی تو آقا پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اس کی پوری قیمت دونوں ولیوں کو آدھی آدھی دے اور پھر غاصب سے پوری قیمت وصول کرے اور پوری قیمت میں سے نصف ولی جنایت اولی کو دے دے ۔ سے واپس اولیٰ کو دیدے اور یہ نصف جو اس نے ولی جنایت اولی کو دی ہے اس کو پھر غاصب سے واپس لے اور بقول اصبح اس میں امام محمد کا بھی اتفاق ہے یعنی وہ بھی یہی فرماتے ہیں اور باقی بات واضح ہے۔
Whoever usurped a mudabbir, and the mudabbir committed jinaayah at the usurper's, then he returned him to the master, then he usurped him again, then he committed another jinaayah at the usurper's, then the master owes his value which is half-and-half between them. He said: And whoever usurps a mudabbir, and he commits a jinaayah at his place, then he returns him to the master, then he usurps him, then he commits a jinaayah at his place, then the master owes his value between them half-and-half because he restricted a single body (raqabah) by tadbir, so one value is obligatory. Then the master recovers his full value from the usurper because both jinaayat were in the usurper's hand. Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever usurps a mudabbir, and he commits jinaayah at the usurper's, then he returns him to the master, then he usurps him, then he commits jinaayah at his place, then the master owes his value, which will be half-and-half between the two (victims), because the master restricted a single body by tadbir, so one value is obligatory. Then the master recovers his full value from the usurper because both jinaayat occurred in the usurper's hand. Explanation: If the usurper usurped a mudabbir and the mudabbir committed jinaayah at the usurper's, and the usurper returned him to his master (sayyid), and then usurped him again, and the mudabbir committed another jinaayah at the usurper's, then the master is obligated to give the full value half-and-half to both walis, then recover the full value from the usurper, and from the full value give half to the wali of the first jinaayah. And return the first, and this half which he gave to the wali of the first jinaayah, he takes it back from the usurper. And by the saying of the ashab (al-as-hab), Imam Muhammad also agrees, i.e., he also says this. And the rest is clear.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Muhammad's ruling on a mudabbir (a slave promised emancipation upon master's death) who commits two jinaayat, both while in the possession of a usurper, but with an intervening return to the master and a second usurpation. The scenario: Usurper takes the mudabbir, the mudabbir commits first jinaayah at the usurper's; the usurper returns him to the master; then the usurper takes him again (second usurpation), and the mudabbir commits a second jinaayah at the usurper's. The ruling: The master owes the full value (diyat value) of the mudabbir, to be divided equally between the two victims (half to the first victim, half to the second). The reason given is that the master, by virtue of tadbir (the contract of emancipation upon death), has restricted the mudabbir's raqabah (body/capital) from being sold; therefore, he is obliged to pay a single value (because the mudabbir cannot be handed over, only his value). Then the master recovers the full value from the usurper because both jinaayat occurred in the usurper's possession. The commentary (tashrih) clarifies that the master pays the full value to both walis (half each), then recovers the full value from the usurper. Out of the recovered full value, the master gives half to the first victim (as compensation for the first jinaayah), and then the master can recover that half again from the usurper (since the usurper is ultimately liable). The passage also notes that Imam Muhammad agrees with this ruling (it is not disputed between him and the two shaykhs).

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave whom the master has promised to emancipate upon his death; this is a tadbir contract.
رقبة (raqabah): The body or capital of the slave; refers to the slave as a property unit.
تخبير (tadbir): The legal act of making a mudabbir, i.e., a slave promised emancipation after the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the master restricted the mudabbir's raqabah by tadbir, so one value is obligatory
C) Because the usurper is liable for both
D) Because the two jinaayat are considered one act

Key Takeaway
When a mudabbir commits multiple jinayat while in a usurper's possession, the master pays one value (divided among victims) and recovers the full value from the usurper.

Master's Recourse When a Mudabbir's Tort Occurs Successively in Usurper's Possession
Commentary on mudabbir's successive torts and master's recourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the master's liability and recoupment when a mudabbir commits two successive torts in the usurper's possession, distinguish the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad's positions, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Master pays half to each victim, recoups full value from usurper, then keeps half after compensating the first victim.

This lesson examines a nuanced case from the Book of Diyat: a mudabbir (slave promised freedom upon master's death) is wrongfully seized by a usurper (ghāṣib). While in the usurper's possession, the mudabbir commits a tort against one person. The usurper returns him to the master, then seizes him again, and during this second period the mudabbir commits another tort against a different person. The master is liable to compensate both victims, but he also has a right of recourse against the usurper. The precise allocation of the recouped amount sparks an instructive intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the rule established by the Shaykhayn: the master must pay the full value of the mudabbir to the two victims equally (half each). Then the master recoups the full value from the usurper. Out of that recouped sum, the master gives half to the first victim (who originally was entitled to the whole value before the second tort) and keeps the other half.
The master's right of recourse is based on the fact that both torts occurred in the usurper's possession.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the view of Imam Muhammad: he holds that the master recoups only half the value from the usurper and keeps that half for himself, without giving any additional payment to the first victim. However, later clarification suggests that Imam Muhammad agrees with the Shaykhayn in this specific scenario because the second tort also occurred in the usurper's possession.
The disagreement turns on whether the recouped amount duplicates the first victim's right.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (dalīl)
For the Shaykhayn: since both torts were in the usurper's hand, the master can recoup the entire value. The first victim's right was entire before competition, so half of the recouped sum goes to him; the second victim's right is only half due to precedence, so the remaining half is kept by the master as compensation for his payment to the second victim. Imam Muhammad's original principle: if the second tort had occurred in the master's possession, recoupment would duplicate the first victim's entitlement. Here, because the second tort was also in the usurper's possession, the recouped amount can be designated as compensation for the second tort, avoiding duplication.
The commentator emphasizes that Imam Muhammad's distinction avoids circularity.
4
Determine the tarjīḥ (preferred view)
The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) states that the sound opinion (qawl al-ṣaḥīḥ) is that Imam Muhammad agrees with the Shaykhayn in this case. Thus, the operative ruling for fatwa is the position of the Shaykhayn: master pays half to each victim, recoups full value, gives half to first victim, and keeps the rest.
The authority weight is Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.
5
Apply the thanmarah al-khilāf (practical consequence)
Under the Shaykhayn's view, the master ends up with a net financial benefit (he keeps half the value after compensating both victims). Under Imam Muhammad's strict view (if applied), the master would only recoup half and keep it, resulting in a smaller benefit. In this case, the difference is resolved by agreement, so the master's net gain is the same.
This case illustrates how competing claims and recourse interact.

Source Text
