۳۱۳ كتاب الديات اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ جنایت کی پھر غاصب نے اس کو واپس کر دیا پس اس نے دوسری جنایت کی پس مولی اس کو دونوں ولی جنایت کو دیدے گا پھر غاصب سے اس کی نصف قیمت واپس لے گا پس اس کو اول کی جانب دیدے گا اور اس کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا اور یہ شیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور محمد نے فرمایا کہ نصف قیمت کے بارے میں رجوع کرے گا پس وہ آقا کے لئے محفوظ رہے گی ۔ اور اگر اس نے آقا کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اس کو غصب کیا ہو پس اس کے قبضہ میں اس نے جنایت کی تو آقا غلام کو آدھا آدھا دیدے گا اور آقا اس کی نصف قیمت کے بارے میں رجوع کرے گا ( غاصب پر ) پس اس کو اوّل کو دیدگا اور اس کے بارے میں رجوع نہیں کرے گا اور جواب غلام کے بارے میں مدبر کے جواب کے مثل ہے ان تمام صورتوں میں جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہیں مگر اس صورت میں آقا غلام کو دے گا اور پہلی میں قیمت کو ۔ تشریح اس ساری تفصیل کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر بجائے مدبر کے غلام ہو تو تب بھی یہی تفصیل اور اختلاف ہے لیکن اتنا فرق ہے کہ غلام کی صورت میں غلام دینا پڑتا ہے اور مدبر کی صورت میں اس کی قیمت اور باقی صورت وہی ہے جو پہلے مسئلہ کی تھی لیکن امام محمد نے مدبر کا بیان کر کے پھر اس کو بھی بیان فرمایا ہے اس لئے امام محمد کے طرز کے مطابق مصنف نے یہی طریقہ اختیار فرمایا ہے۔ جس نے مدبر کو غصب کیا مدبرنے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اسے مولیٰ کی طرف لوٹا دیا پھر اسے غصب کیا پھر دوسری جنایت غاصب کے پاس کی مولیٰ پر اس کی قیمت ہے جو دونوں کے درمیان نصف نصف ہوگی

قال ومن غصب مدبرا فجنى عنده جناية ثم رده على المولى ثم غصبه ثم جنى عنده جناية فعلى المولى قیمته بينهما نصفان لأنه منع رقبة واحدة بالتدبير فتجب عليه قيمة واحدة ثم يرجع بقيمته على الغاصب لأن الجنايتين كانتا في يد الغاصب

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے مدبر کو غصب کیا پس اس نے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی پھر اس کو مولی کو واپس کر دیا پھر اس کو غصب کیا پھر اس کے پاس جنایت کی تو مولیٰ پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے جو ان دونوں کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہو گی اس لئے کہ آقا نے تدبیر کی وجہ سے ایک رقبہ کو روکا ہے تو اس پر ایک قیمت واجب ہے پھر آقا اس کی پوری قیمت کے بارے میں غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا اس لئے کہ دونوں جنایتین غاصب کے قبضہ میں ہوئی ہیں ۔ تشریح اگر غاصب نے مدبر غصب کیا اور مدبرنے غاصب کے پاس جنایت کی اور غاصب نے سید بر آقا کو واپس کر دیا اور پھر دوبارہ غصب کر لیا اور مدبر نے غاصب کے پاس دوبارہ پھر جنایت کی تو آقا پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اس کی پوری قیمت دونوں ولیوں کو آدھی آدھی دے اور پھر غاصب سے پوری قیمت وصول کرے اور پوری قیمت میں سے نصف ولی جنایت اولی کو دے دے ۔ سے واپس اولیٰ کو دیدے اور یہ نصف جو اس نے ولی جنایت اولی کو دی ہے اس کو پھر غاصب سے واپس لے اور بقول اصبح اس میں امام محمد کا بھی اتفاق ہے یعنی وہ بھی یہی فرماتے ہیں اور باقی بات واضح ہے۔

كتاب الديات ۳۱۴ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ آقا نصف قیمت اول ولی جنایت کو دے گا

فيدفع نصفها إلى الأول لأنه استحق كل القيمة لأن عند وجود الجناية عليه لا حق لغيره وإنما انتقص بحكم المزاحمة من بعد.

ترجمہ پس آقا قیمت کا نصف اول کو دیدے اس لئے کہ پوری قیمت کا مستحق ہوا تھا اس لئے کہ اول پر جنایت کے پائے جانے کے وقت اس کے غیر کا حق نہیں تھا اور اول کا حق گھٹا ہے بعد میں مزاحمت کے حکم سے۔ تشریح اس کی توضیح واضح ہے اور ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے۔

آقا غاصب پر رجوع کرے گا

قال ويرجع به على الغاصب لأن الاستحقاق بسبب كان فى يده ويسلم له ولا يدفعه إلى ولى الجناية الأولى ولا إلى ولى الجناية الثانية لأنه لا حق له إلا في النصف لسبق حق الأول وقد وصل ذلك إليه ثم قيل هذه المسألة على الاختلاف كالأولى وقيل على الاتفاق

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور اس نصف کو غاصب سے واپس لے لے اس لئے کہ استحقاق اس سبب سے ہوا ہے جو غاصب کے قبضہ میں ہوا تھا اور یہ نصف آقا کے لئے سالم رہے گا۔ اور آقا اس کو ولی جنایت اولی اور ثانیہ کو نہیں دے گا۔ اس لئے کہ ثانی کا تو حق ہی نصف کے اندر ہے اول کے حق کے مقدم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ نصف اس کی جانب پہنچ چکا ہے پھر کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ مثل اول کے اختلاف پر ہے اور کیا گیا ہے کہ اتفاق پر ہے۔ تشریح یعنی دوبارہ جو نصف آقانے ولی جنایت اولی کو دیا ہے اس کو غاصب سے پھر واپس لے لے اور اب جو کچھ ہے وہ سب آقا کا ہوگا اس لئے کہ اول کا جو حق تھا وہ پورا اس کو مل چکا ہے اور ثانی کا حق تو تھا ہی نصف کیونکہ مزاحمت ہے۔ پھر سوال یہ ہے کہ اس میں امام محمد کا اتفاق ہے یا اختلاف ہے؟ قول اصبح یہی ہے کہ اتفاق ہے، اب سوال ہو گا کہ امام محمد اپنے اصول سے کیوں ہٹے ۔ اور پہلے مسئلہ اور اس میں فرق کیا تو آگے اس وجہ فرق کو واضح کرتے ہیں۔

امام محمد کا دونوں صورتوں میں فرق کرنے کی وجہ

والفرق لمحمد أن فى الأولى الذى يرجع به عوض عما سلم لولى الجناية الأولى لأن الجناية الثانية كانت فى يد المالك فلو دفع إليه ثانيا يتكرر الاستحقاق أما فى هذه المسألة فيمكن أن يجعل عوضا عن الجناية الثانية لحصولها فى يد الغاصب فلايؤدى إلى ما ذكــر نــــاه ترجمہ اور وجہ فرق مجد کے لئے یہ ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں وہ مقدار جس کو مولیٰ غاصب سے واپس لیتا ہے وہ عوض ہے۔ اس چیز کا جو مولی نے ولی جنایت اولی کو دیا ہے اس لئے کہ جنایت ثانیہ مالک کے قبضہ میں ہوئی ہے پس اگر ولی اول کو دوبارہ دیدیا تو استحقاق مکر رہو جائے گا بہر حال اس مسئلہ میں پس ممکن ہے کہ اس کو جنایت ثانیہ کا عوض قرار دیدیا جائے جنایت ثانیہ کے حاصل ہونے کی وجہ سے غاصب
Page 313: Book of Diyat. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 15. ... Then the usurper returned it to him, then he committed another tort. So the master will give him to both guardians of the tort, then he will take back half its value from the usurper, then he will give it to the first, and regarding it he will have recourse against the usurper. And this is according to the two shaykhs. And Muhammad said that he will have recourse regarding half the value, so it will remain preserved for the master. And if he committed a tort while with the master, then he was usurped, then he committed a tort in his possession, then the master will give the slave half and half, and the master will have recourse regarding half its value against the usurper, so he will give it to the first and will not have recourse regarding it. And the answer regarding the slave is like the answer regarding the mudabbir in all these cases which we have mentioned, except that in this case the master will give the slave, and in the first he will give the value. Commentary: The summary of all this detail is that if instead of a mudabbir there is a slave, then also this same detail and dispute applies, but the difference is that in the case of a slave, the slave must be given, and in the case of a mudabbir, his value. And the rest of the case is the same as the previous issue. But Imam Muhammad mentioned the mudabbir and then also mentioned this, so according to Imam Muhammad's style, the author adopted this method. Whoever usurped a mudabbir, the mudabbir committed a tort in the presence of the usurper, then he returned him to the master, then he usurped him, then he committed a second tort in the presence of the usurper. Upon the master is his value, which is half and half between the two. He said: And whoever usurps a mudabbir, and he commits a tort in his presence, then returns him to the master, then usurps him, then commits a tort in his presence, then upon the master is his value between them, half and half, because he restrained one neck by tadbir, so one value is due upon him. Then he will have recourse with his value against the usurper, because both torts were in the hand of the usurper. Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever usurped a mudabbir, then he committed a tort in the presence of the usurper, then he returned him to the master, then he usurped him, then he committed a tort in his presence, then upon the master is his value due, which is half and half between these two, because the master restrained one neck by tadbir, so one value is due upon him. Then the master will have recourse for his full value against the usurper, because both torts were in the possession of the usurper. Commentary: If the usurper usurped the mudabbir and the mudabbir committed a tort in the presence of the usurper, and the usurper returned him to the master, and then again usurped him, and the mudabbir again committed a tort in the presence of the usurper, then it is obligatory upon the master that he give his full value to both guardians half and half, and then recover the full value from the usurper, and from the full value give half to the guardian of the first tort. ... and take back that half from the usurper, and according to the sound opinion, Imam Muhammad agrees with this, i.e., he also says the same. And the rest is clear. [Page 315] The master gives half of the value to the first guardian. So he gives half of it to the first because he was entitled to the full value, because at the time of the tort's occurrence upon him, no one else had a right; it only decreased by the rule of later competition. Translation: So the master gives half of the value to the first, because he was entitled to the full value, because at the time of the tort's occurrence upon him, there was no right for anyone else, and his right decreased only by the rule of later competition. Commentary: Its clarification is clear and has passed before. The master will have recourse against the usurper. He said: And he will have recourse with it against the usurper, because the entitlement was due to a reason that was in his hand, and it remains safe for him, and he will not give it to the guardian of the first or second tort, because the second has no right except in half due to the precedence of the first's right, and that half has reached him. Then it was said: This issue is upon difference like the first, and it was said: upon agreement. Translation: Muhammad said: And he will take back this half from the usurper, because the entitlement was due to a reason that occurred in the possession of the usurper, and this half will remain safe for the master. And the master will not give it to the guardian of the first or second tort, because the second's right is only in half due to the precedence of the first's right, and that half has reached him. Then it was said: This issue is upon difference like the first, and it was said: upon agreement. Commentary: That is, the half that the master gave to the guardian of the first tort, he will again take it back from the usurper, and now whatever remains is all the master's, because the first's right has been fully fulfilled, and the second's right was only half due to competition. Then the question is: In this, does Imam Muhammad agree or differ? The sound opinion is that there is agreement. Now the question will be: Why did Imam Muhammad deviate from his principle? And what is the difference between the first issue and this? So ahead they clarify the reason for the difference. The reason for Imam Muhammad's distinction between the two cases. And the distinction for Muhammad is that in the first, what he has recourse with is the compensation for what was delivered to the guardian of the first tort, because the second tort was in the hand of the owner; so if he gives it again to the second, the entitlement would be repeated. However, in this issue, it is possible to make it compensation for the second tort because it occurred in the hand of the usurper, so it does not lead to what was mentioned. Translation: And the reason for the distinction for Muhammad is that in the first case, the amount which the master takes back from the usurper is compensation for what the master gave to the guardian of the first tort, because the second tort occurred in the possession of the owner. So if he gives it again to the first, the entitlement would be repeated. However, in this issue, it is possible to make it compensation for the second tort due to its occurrence in the hand of the usurper, so it does not lead to what was mentioned.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents an intricate case from the Book of Diyat concerning a mudabbir (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death) who is wrongfully seized (ghaṣb) by a usurper. While in the usurper's possession, the mudabbir commits a tort against one person. The usurper then returns the mudabbir to the master, only to seize him again, and in this second period of possession, the mudabbir commits another tort against a different person. The legal question is: How is the master liable, and what recourse does he have against the usurper?

The passage first states the ruling according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): the master must pay the full value of the mudabbir to the two victims, dividing it equally (half to each). The master then recoups the entire value from the usurper. From the amount recouped, the master gives half to the first victim (since the first victim's right was entire before the second tort competed) and the remaining half stays with the master (because the second victim's right was only half due to the first's precedence). Imam Muhammad differs: he holds that the master recoups only half the value from the usurper, and that half remains with the master (no additional payment to the first victim). However, a later clarification suggests that Imam Muhammad agrees with the Shaykhayn in this particular scenario, because the second tort also occurred in the usurper's possession, allowing the recouped amount to be considered compensation for the second tort, avoiding duplication of entitlement. The essential difference between the two cases (this one versus a previous case where the second tort occurred in the master's possession) is that if the second tort was in the master's possession, recoupment would duplicate the first victim's right; here, since both torts occurred in the usurper's possession, the recouped amount can justifiably be kept by the master as compensation for the second tort. The author of the commentary (Ashraf al-Hidayah) clarifies that the relied-upon opinion is that Imam Muhammad agrees in this case.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave who has been promised by his master that he will be free upon the master's death; he is in a state of tadbīr.
غصب (ghaṣb): Unlawful seizure of property (here, the mudabbir) without right.
جنایت (jinaayah): A tort or crime causing bodily harm; here specifically a crime against a person that necessitates blood money (diyah).
ولی جنایت (wali jinaayah): The legal guardian or heir of the victim entitled to claim diyah (blood money).
مولیٰ (mawla): Master; the owner of the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn in this passage, what does the master do with the amount he recoups from the ghāṣib?
A) He gives the entire recouped amount to the first victim.
B) He gives half to the first victim and keeps the other half.
C) He gives half to each victim.
D) He keeps the entire amount for himself.

Key Takeaway
When a mudabbir commits two torts in the usurper's possession, the master pays half the value to each victim, recoups the full value from the usurper, gives half of that to the first victim, and keeps the other half as compensation for his payment to the second victim.

8 min
Master's Recovery from Usurper: Imam Muhammad's Distinction
Expands on a intra-Hanafi dispute about master's recovery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Muhammad distinguishes two cases of a master recovering half the price from a usurper, and apply the rationale to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
Master's recovery from usurper is compensation for the second injury, not a refund of the first payment.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a master who pays half the value of a slave to the first guardian (wali) and then recovers that half from a usurper (ghāṣib). The key question is whether Imam Muhammad's ruling in this case is consistent with his earlier ruling in a similar case. We will explore the rationale behind his distinction, which hinges on the location of the second injury.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the master's initial action
Identify the facts: a slave is injured by two persons; the first injury occurs, then the slave is usurped, and a second injury occurs in the usurper's hand. The master pays half the value to the first wali, then recovers that half from the usurper.
The half paid to the first wali is due to competition (muzāḥamah) reducing the first wali's claim from full to half.
2
Identify the dispute
The dispute is whether Imam Muhammad's ruling in this case is the same as his earlier ruling in a case where the second injury occurred in the owner's possession. Some say it is different (ikhtilāf), others say it is consistent (ittifāq).
The correct view (asahh) according to the text is agreement (ittifāq).
3
Analyze the difference in location of the second injury
In the first case, the second injury occurred in the owner's hand (the slave was in the owner's possession). In this case, the second injury occurred in the usurper's hand.
The location of the second injury is the key variable that changes the legal character of the recovery.
4
Understand Imam Muhammad's reasoning
Imam Muhammad argues that in the first case, if the master recovered the half and gave it to the first wali again, there would be repetition of entitlement (takrār al-istihqāq). In this case, the recovered amount can be treated as compensation for the second injury because it occurred in the usurper's possession, thus avoiding repetition.
The recovery is not a refund but compensation for the second injury, so it belongs to the master.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical outcome)
The practical result is that the master keeps the recovered half and does not pay it to either wali. This is consistent with Imam Muhammad's principle that repetition of entitlement must be avoided.
The ruling is muftā bihi and based on the soundest view.

Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex scenario within the Hanafi school involving the master (aqa) who has paid half the value of a slave to the first wali (guardian of the first injury) and then recovers that half from the usurper (ghāṣib). The commentary expands on Imam Muhammad's ruling that the master recovers the half from the usurper and keeps it, not paying it to either wali. It then discusses whether Imam Muhammad's position in this case is in agreement or difference with his earlier ruling in a similar case. The text clarifies that the difference lies in the location of the second injury: in the earlier case, the second injury occurred in the owner's possession, causing repetition of entitlement if the master paid the first wali again; here, the second injury occurred in the usurper's possession, allowing the recovered amount to be treated as compensation for the second injury, avoiding repetition. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the underlying reasoning.

Key Terms
ولي (walī): Guardian of the victim entitled to claim blood money or retaliation
غاصب (ghāṣib): Usurper who forcibly takes possession of a free person or property unlawfully
مزاحمة (muzāḥamah): Competition between two claimants reducing each one's share
عوض (ʿiwaḍ): Compensation; in this context, the recovery is treated as compensation for the second injury
تكرار الاستحقاق (takrār al-istihqāq): Repetition of entitlement; a legal defect avoided by Imam Muhammad's distinction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Muhammad treat the second case differently from the first case regarding the master's recovery from the usurper?
A) Because the first injury occurred in the owner's hand
B) Because the second injury occurred in the owner's hand
C) Because the second injury occurred in the usurper's hand, allowing the recovery to be compensation for it
D) Because the master had already paid the full value

Key Takeaway
The master's recovery from the usurper is compensation for the second injury occurring in his hand, not a refund of the first payment, thus preventing any repetition of entitlement.

Usurper's Liability for Diya: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Ruling on usurper's liability with istihsan vs qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school imposes diya on the usurper's aqila for unnatural death but not natural death, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Zufar counter-argument.

Core Idea
The usurper's control over a free child creates liability by istihsan for preventable deaths, not for inevitable ones.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling on usurpation (ghasb) of a free child. The school distinguishes between natural death (e.g., sudden illness) — no liability — and unnatural death (e.g., snakebite) — diya on the usurper's aqila. This distinction, justified by istihsan (juristic preference), diverges from the strict qiyas that would absolve liability entirely. We will unpack the reasoning, the opposing view of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what act is being ruled upon (usurpation of a free child) and the two possible rulings depending on cause of death: natural death (no liability) vs unnatural death (diya on aqila).
The ruling is not monolithic; it bifurcates based on the type of death.
2
State the Hanafi proof (istihsan)
Recognize that the Hanafi position relies on istihsan, which overrides the clear analogy (qiyas jali). Understand why istihsan is invoked: the usurper's control is considered a proximate cause of exposure to unnatural harms.
Istihsan is a recognized source in Hanafi usul, allowing departure from strict analogy for a stronger consideration.
3
Examine the opposing proof (qiyas)
Analyze the qiyas argument made by Zufar and al-Shafi'i: usurpation of a free person is not legally established (ghasb al-hurr la yatahaqqaq), so by analogy with a minor mukatib, there should be no liability at all.
The analogy rests on the attribute of freedom (hurriya) in both person (raqaba) and possession (yad).
4
Analyze the qiyas panel structure
Break down the qiyas: asl = minor mukatib (no liability), far = free child, illa = freedom (hurriya) in both aspects. The Hanafi response uses istihsan to break the analogy by distinguishing causation types.
The illa in qiyas is jaliyyah, but istihsan introduces a khafi (hidden) consideration.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of the difference: under Hanafi law, the usurper's aqila pays diya for unnatural deaths; under Shafi'i/Zufar, no payment at all. This affects the child's family's right to blood money.
The thamarah al-khilaf is concrete: whether or not the aqila pays diya.

کسی نے آزاد بچہ کو نصب کیا اور وہ بچہ غاصب کے پاس نا گہانی موت سے یا بخار سے مر گیا تو غاصب پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اور اگر سانپ کے ڈسنے اور بجلی گرنے سے مرا تو غاصب کی عاقلہ پر دیت ہے
قال ومن غصب صبيا حرا فمات في يده فجأة أو بحمى فليس عليه شيء وإن مات من صاعقة أو نهسة حية فعلى عاقلة الغاصب الدية وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يضمن فى الوجهين وهو قول زفر والشافعي لأن الغصب فى الحر لا يتحقق الايرى أنه لو كان مكاتبا صغيرا لا يضمن مع أنه حريدا فإذا كان الصغير حرا رقبة ويدا أولى
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے آزاد بچہ کو غصب کیا تو وہ غاصب کے قبضہ میں نا گہانی موت سے یا بخار سے مر گیا تو اس پر کچھ نہ ہوگا اور اگر بجلی گرنے سے یا سانپ کے ڈسنے سے مرا ہو تو غاصب کے عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہے اور یہ استحسان ہے اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ وہ دونوں صورتوں میں ضامن نہ ہو اور یہی زفر اور شافعی کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ آزاد کا غصب متحقق نہیں ہوتا کیا یہ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر مکاتب صغیر ہو تو غاصب ضامن نہیں ہوتا، باوجود اس بات کہ وہ (مکاتب صغیر ) قبضہ کے اعتبار سے آزاد ہے پس جب کہ صغیر آزاد ہے رقبہ اور ید دونوں اعتبار سے تو بدرجہ اولی ( غاصب ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ )
Someone usurped a free child and that child died in the usurper's possession by sudden death or fever: nothing upon him. And if he died by lightning or snakebite, the diya is upon the usurper's aqila. He (Muhammad) said: And whoever usurps a free child and he dies in his hand unexpectedly or by fever, nothing upon him. And if he dies by lightning or snakebite, upon the usurper's aqila is the diya. This is istihsan. And by qiyas, he is not liable in both cases, and this is the saying of Zufar and Shafi'i, because the usurpation of a free person is not realized. Do you not see that if it is a minor mukatib, he is not liable even though he is free in terms of possession? So if the minor is free in terms of person and possession, then all the more reason (the usurper is not liable).
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school (Imam Muhammad) regarding a free child who is usurped (taken by force) and dies while in the usurper's custody. The ruling distinguishes between two types of death: natural/sudden death (e.g., sudden illness, fever) — no liability; and unnatural death (lightning, snakebite) — diya (blood money) is due on the usurper's 'aqila (tribal group/family responsible for paying diya). The Hanafi position relies on istihsan (juristic preference), while the qiyas (analogy) would lead to no liability in either case. The opposing view (Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i) argues that usurpation of a free person is not established (because a free person is not owned, so taking them is not true usurpation in the sense that creates liability). They draw an analogy with a minor mukatib (a slave who has contracted manumission), where no liability is imposed. The Hanafi istihsan prefers to impose liability for violent or unnatural deaths to protect the child's life, considering the usurper's control a cause of death.

Key Terms
غصب (ghaṣb): Taking property or a person by force and without right, creating liability (daman) for damages
عاقلة (ʿāqilah): The group on whose behalf blood money is paid, typically the male relatives (asaba) of the offender
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; setting aside a clear analogy for a stronger consideration (e.g., public interest or ease)
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has made a contract of manumission (kitaba) with his master, paying installments for freedom

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when does the usurper of a free child become liable for diya?
A) When the child dies suddenly or by fever
B) When the child dies by lightning or snakebite
C) In all cases of death
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to impose liability on the usurper's aqila for unnatural deaths of a free child, while qiyas would exempt him entirely.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate

Usurper's Liability for Transferring Child to Dangerous Place
Hanafi istihsan proof for liability in indirect killing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a condition with transgression takes the ruling of a cause, and apply it to scenarios of indirect killing (tasbib).

Core Idea
A transgressor's act that creates a condition for harm makes him liable as if he caused it directly.

This passage from the Hidayah explores a nuanced point in Hanafi tort law: when does an indirect act (tasbib) create liability? The specific case is a usurper who moves a child to a place where lightning or beasts are common. The author uses istihsan to argue that the transgression elevates the condition to the level of a cause. Let's unpack this reasoning and see how it connects to the famous example of digging a well on a public road.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What act is being ruled upon, and what is the hukm? The act: a usurper moves a child to a dangerous place (e.g., where lightning or beasts are common). The ruling: the usurper is liable for blood money (diyah) on his 'āqilah because his act is a cause (tasbib) of the child's death.
2
Locate the dalil
What is the proof for this ruling? The proof is istihsan (juristic preference), not direct textual evidence. The author cites the principle that a condition (shart) of a cause, when combined with transgression (ta‘addī), takes the ruling of the cause itself.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the analogy work? The original case: digging a well on a public road. The well is a condition for harm; the digger is liable because he transgressed (no permission). Similarly, moving the child to a dangerous place is a condition; the usurper's transgression (taking without permission) makes him liable. The 'illa (effective cause) is the combination of transgression and condition.
The analogy is qiyas khafi (implicit analogy) because the link is not obvious without istihsan.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is this ruling universally accepted? Other madhhabs may not accept istihsan as a valid proof; they might require direct causation (mubasharah) for liability. Within the Hanafi school, istihsan is a recognized source, so this ruling stands.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? In the Hanafi view, the usurper's 'āqilah must pay diyah. In other schools, if they reject istihsan, the usurper might not be liable at all unless directly killing, leading to no blood money.

احناف کی استحسانی دلیل

وجه الاستحسان أنه لا يضمن بالغصب ولكن يضمن بالإتلاف وهذا إتلاف تسبيبا لأنه نقله إلى أرض مسبعة أو إلى مكان الصواعق وهذا لأن الصواعق والحيات والسباع لاتكون في كل مكان فإذا نقله إليه وهو متعد فيه وقد أزال حفظ الولى فيضاف إليه لأن شرط العلة ينزل منزلة العلة إذا كان تعديا كالحفر في الطريق بخلاف الموت فجأة أو بحمى لأن ذلك لا يختلف باختلاف الأماكن حتى لو نقله إلى موضع يغلب فيه الحمى والأمراض نقول بأنه يضمن فتجب الدية على العاقلة لكونه قتلا تسبيبا

ترجمہ استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غاصب غصب کرنے کی وجہ سے مضامین نہیں ہوتا لیکن وہ اختلاف کی وجہ سے ضامن ہوتا ہے اور یہ بطور سبب کے اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ غاصب نے اس کو ایسی جگہ منتقل کیا جہاں درندے بکثرت ہیں اور یا بجلیاں بکثرت گرتی ہیں اور یہ اس لئے کہ بجلیاں اور سانپ اور درندے ہر جگہ نہیں ہوتے پس جب اس کو وہاں لے گیا اور غاصب اس سے نقل کرنے میں متعدی ہے حالانکہ غاصب نے ولی کی حفاظت کو زائل کر دیا تو اتلاف غاصب کی طرف مضاف ہوگا اس لئے کہ علت کی شرط کو جب کہ شرط بطور تعدی کے ہو علت کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جاتا ہے جیسے راستہ میں کنواں کھودنا بخلاف گہانی موت یا بخار کی وجہ سے موت کے اس لئے کہ یہ ( نا گہانی موت اور بخار کی وجہ سے ) مختلف نہیں ہوتی جگہوں کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس کو ایسی جگہ لے گیا جہاں بخار اور امراض

پھیلے ہوئے ہیں تو ہم کہیں گے کہ وہ ضامن ہوگا تو عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہوا اس کے قتل ہونے کی وجہ سے تسبیا (نہ کہ مباشرة )۔

تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے اور ہمارا مذ ہب استحسان پر مبنی ہے تو استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہم نے غاصب کو جو ضامن بنایا ہے وہ نصب کی وجہ سے نہیں بنایا بلکہ اتلاف کی وجہ سے ضامن بنایا ہے اور غاصب اتلاف کا سبب ہے کیونکہ بجلیاں تمام جگہوں میں نہیں گرتیں اور سانپ اور درندے ہر جگہ نہیں ہوتے تو وہ بچہ کو ایسی جگہ کیوں لے گیا تو اس لے جانے میں وہ متعدی ہے اور بچہ کا ولی اس کی حفاظت کرتا لیکن اس نے ولی کی حفاظت سے بھی اس کو محروم کر دیا ہے اور یہ اصول مقرر ہے کہ شرط کو جب کہ شرط میں تعدی اور زیادتی پائی جائے۔ علت کا درجہ دے کر ضمان واجب کہہ دیا جاتا ہے جیسے کنواں کھودنے میں ایسا ہی ہے لہذا ایسا ہی یہاں ہو گا اور اتلاف غاصب کی طرف مضاف ہوگا اور نا گہانی موت سے مرنایا بخار سے مرنا سب جگہ ہوتا تو اس میں نقل و انتقال کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے لہذا اس صورت میں غاصب ضامین نہ ہوگا۔

البتہ اگر غاصب بچہ کو ایسی جگہ لے گیا جہاں بخار یا دیگر امراض پھیلے ہوئے ہیں تو اب غاصب ضائن ہو گا اور دیت واجب ہو گی لیکن سیدیت عاقلہ پر ہوگی غاصب پر نہیں کیونکہ غاصب نے بذات خود قتل نہیں کیا بلکہ وہ قتل کا سبب بنا ہے۔

تنبیہ ! یہاں غصب سے مراد بچہ کے ولی کی اجازت کے بغیر اپنے ساتھ لے جانا ہے۔
Book of Blood Money. Hanafi istihsan proof: The justification of istihsan is that one is not liable for usurpation (ghasb) but is liable for destruction (itlaf). This is destruction by causation because he moved him to a land abounding in beasts or to a place of lightning, because lightning, snakes, and beasts are not in every place. So when he moved him there and he is transgressing in that, and he has removed the guardian's protection, it is attributed to him because the condition of the cause takes the ruling of the cause when there is transgression, like digging a well in the road. Unlike sudden death or death by fever, because that does not vary by location. If he moved him to a place where fever and diseases prevail, we say he is liable; thus blood money is obligatory on the ‘āqilah because it is killing by causation. Translation: The istihsan proof is that the usurper is not liable due to usurpation but is liable due to destruction, and this is destruction by causation because he transferred the child to a place with many beasts or lightning. Since lightning, snakes, and beasts are not everywhere, his act is transgressive, and he has removed the guardian's protection, so the destruction is attributed to him. The principle is that a condition of the cause, when accompanied by transgression, takes the ruling of the cause, as in digging a well. Contrast with sudden death or fever, which are not location-dependent. If he moved the child to a place with prevalent fever or diseases, we rule he is liable, and blood money is on the ‘āqilah because it is killing by causation (tasbib) not directly. Explanation: This is our proof, and our school is based on istihsan. The proof of istihsan is that we made the usurper liable not due to usurpation but due to destruction, and the usurper is a cause of destruction. Because lightning does not fall everywhere, and snakes and beasts are not everywhere, why did he take the child there? In that taking he is transgressive, and the child's guardian was protecting him, but he deprived him of that protection. The established principle is that when a condition involves transgression and excess, it is given the status of a cause, making liability wajib. The same applies here, and the destruction is attributed to the usurper. Sudden death or death from fever occur everywhere, so transfer makes no difference; in that case the usurper is not liable. However, if the usurper took the child to a place where fever or other diseases are prevalent, then the usurper is liable and blood money is wajib, but on the ‘āqilah, not on the usurper, because he did not kill directly but was a cause. Note: Here 'usurpation' means taking the child without the guardian's permission.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof (istihsan). The author explains why a usurper (ghasib) who takes a child to a dangerous place (e.g., where lightning or beasts are common) is liable for the child's death, even though he did not directly kill. The key principle is that a condition (shart) of a cause, when combined with transgression (ta‘addī), takes the ruling of the cause itself. The example given is digging a well on a public road: the hole (a condition) is not the direct cause of death, but because the digger transgressed, he is liable. Similarly, the usurper's act of moving the child to a dangerous place is a transgression, and the child's death is attributed to him. However, if the death would have occurred anyway (e.g., sudden death or fever that is not location-specific), the usurper is not liable. An exception is if the child dies from a disease prevalent at the new location; then liability applies because the act of moving was transgressive. The ruling is that blood money (diyah) is paid by the ‘āqilah (tribal surety) because it is killing by causation (tasbib), not directly. The passage also clarifies that 'usurpation' here means taking without the guardian's permission.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Taking a child without the guardian's permission (as clarified in the tanbih).
إتلاف (itlāf): Destruction of property or life, here by causation (tasbib) rather than directly.
تسبيب (tasbīb): Causing an effect indirectly; the act is not the immediate cause but sets the stage for the harm.
شرط العلة (sharṭ al-‘illa): A condition that is necessary for the cause to operate; here, the dangerous location is the condition for the death.
تعدي (ta‘addī): Transgression; acting without right or exceeding the bounds of permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a usurper (ghasib) liable for blood money (diyah) when a child he kidnapped dies from lightning in a new location?
A) Because he directly killed the child with lightning.
B) Because his act of transgression (taking the child without permission) combined with the condition of the dangerous location makes him a cause of death.
C) Because he is liable for any harm that befalls a child under his control, regardless of transgression.
D) Because lightning is a direct result of his action.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a condition with transgression takes the ruling of a cause, making the transgressor liable for indirect harm (tasbib).

Liability of a Child for Destroying Deposited Property: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on child's liability for depository property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a child's liability for killing a deposited slave versus eating deposited food, explain the reasoning, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A child is liable for killing a deposited slave but not for eating deposited food—direct tort creates liability, consumption does not.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when a child destroys property deposited with him, is he liable? The answer depends on the nature of the act. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, reporting the view of Abu Hanifa and himself, distinguishes between killing a slave (where blood money is due on the 'āqilah) and eating food (where no liability arises). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i disagree, holding liability in both cases. Understanding this dispute refines your grasp of tort liability for minors in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad)
Identify the two cases: killing a deposited slave triggers diyah on the 'āqilah; eating deposited food results in no liability.
This is the position presented first in the matn, indicating it is the relied-upon view.
2
Identify the opposing position
Abu Yusuf (within Hanafi) and al-Shafi'i hold the child liable in both cases—for killing and for eating.
This makes it both an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
The Hanafi view considers killing a direct tort (jinayah) creating liability, while eating is not actionable because the child lacks valid authorization and the act is not a tort. The opposing view treats both as destructive acts causing harm.
The distinction hinges on the legal characterization of the act, not merely the physical result.
4
Note the extension to slaves under interdiction and other transactions
The same difference applies to a slave under interdiction: no immediate liability according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but liability after emancipation; Abu Yusuf holds immediate liability. This extends to loans (iqrad) and loans for use ('ariyah).
The principle of deferring liability until the slave gains capacity runs consistently through these cases.
5
Determine the scope of the dispute
The dispute applies only to a discerning child (sabi qad 'aqal). For a non-discerning child, there is consensus that he is liable because his authorization is invalid and his act is considered.
References to al-Jami' al-Saghir (child who has reason) and al-Jami' al-Kabir (twelve-year-old) clarify the intended subject.

Source Text

بچہ کے پاس غلام ودیعت رکھا گیا بچہ نے اسے قتل کر دیا تو دیت بچہ کی عاقلہ پر ہے اسی طرح اگر کھانا ودیعت رکھا گیا اور بچے نے کھالیا تو بچہ ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء

جمي

قال وإذا أودع صبى عبدا فقتله فعلى عاقلته الدية وإن أودع طعاما فأكله لم يضمن وهذا عند إبى حنيفة ومــحــمد وقال أبويوسف والشافعي ضمن فى الوجهين جـ

ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا اور جب بچہ کے پاس کوئی غلام ودیعت رکھدیا گیا پس بچہ نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو بچہ کے عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہے اور اگر بچہ کے پاس کھانا ودیعت رکھا گیا اس بچہ نے اس کو کھا لیا تو بچہ ضامن نہ ہوگا اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ بچہ دونوں صورتوں میں ضامن ہوگا۔

تشریح اگر کسی بچہ کے پاس کوئی غلام ودیعت رکھا گیا ہو اور بچہ نے اس کوقتل کر دیا ہو تو بچہ کے عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر بچہ کے پاس کھانا ودیعت و امانت رکھا گیا ہو اور بچہ نے اس کو کھا لیا ہو تو طرفین کے نزدیک بچہ پر ضمان نہیں ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک بچہ پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔

مجور علیہ غلام کے پاس مال ودیعت رکھا گیا اس نے ہلاک کر دیا تو ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں

وعلى هذا إذا أودع العبد المحجور عليه مالا فاستهلكه لا يؤاخذ بالضمان في الحال عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ويؤاخذ به بعد العتق وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي يؤاخذ به في الحال وعلى هذا الخلاف الإقراض والإعارة فى العبد والصبي

ترجمہ اور اسی قیاس پر جب کہ غلام مجور علیہ کے پاس کوئی مال ودیعت رکھا گیا ہو پس اس نے اس کو ہلاک کر دیا ہو تو طرفین کے نزدیک غلام فی الحال ضمان میں ماخوذ نہ ہوگا اور عشق کے بعد اس میں ماخوذ ہوگا اور ابو یوسف اور شافعی کے نزدیک اس سے فی الحال مواخذہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی خلاف پر قرض دینا اور عاریت دینا ہے غلام اور بچہ کو۔

تشریح اگر غلام مجور کے پاس کوئی مال امانت رکھا جس کو اس نے ہلاک کر دیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک غلام سے منمان کا مواخذہ بعد معتق ہو گا فی الحال نہ ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک فی الحال مواخذہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح اگر بچہ کو یا غلام مجو کوقرض دیا یا کوئی چیز عاربیت دی اور بچہ نے یا غلام نے اس کو ہلاک کر دیا تو منمان نہ ہوگا البتہ غلام سے بعد عتق مواخذہ ہوگا۔

اختلاف کسی بچہ کے بارے میں ہے اس کا مصداق

وقال محمد في أصل الجامع الصغير صبى قد عقل وفى الجامع الكبير وضع المسألة في صبى ابن اثنتى عشرة سنة وهذا يدل على أن غير العاقل يضمن بالاتفاق لأن التسليط غير معتبر وفعله معتب

ترجمہ اور محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے "صبی قد عقل" اور جامع کبیر میں مسئلہ کو سال کے لڑکے کےبارے میں وضع کیا ہے اور یہ اس بات پر دال ہے کہ غیر عاقل بالا تفاق ضامن ہے اس لئے کہ تسلیط غیر معتبر ہے اور صبی غیر عاقل کا فعل معتبر ہے
A child with whom a slave is deposited and the child kills him: blood money is on the child's 'āqilah. Similarly, if food is deposited and the child eats it, is the child liable or not? Statements of the fuqaha'. (جمي) He (Imam Muhammad) said: If a child is deposed a slave and he kills him, blood money is on his 'āqilah; if food is deposed and he eats it, he is not liable. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: he is liable in both cases. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: When a slave is deposited with a child and the child kills him, blood money is wajib on the child's 'āqilah; if food is deposited and the child eats it, the child is not liable according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said the child is liable in both cases. Explanation: If a slave is deposited with a child and the child kills him, blood money is wajib on the child's 'āqilah; if food is deposited as a trust and the child eats it, according to the two there is no liability, but according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i liability is wajib. A slave under interdiction with whom property is deposited and he destroys it: is he liable or not? And on this basis, if a slave who is under interdiction (mahjur ‘alayh) is deposed property and consumes it, he is not taken to task for liability immediately according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but will be taken after emancipation. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, he is taken immediately. And on this difference are (loans) and (loans for use) concerning the slave and the child. Translation: On the same analogy, when a slave under interdiction is deposed property and he destroys it, the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that he is not immediately liable but will be taken after emancipation; Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold immediate liability. The same difference applies to giving a loan (iqrad) and giving a loan for use (i‘arah) to a slave and a child. Explanation: If a slave under interdiction is given property as a trust and he destroys it, according to the two he is not liable until after emancipation; Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i say immediate liability. Similarly, if a child or a slave under interdiction is given a loan or something as a loan for use and he destroys it, there is no immediate liability; but the slave is liable after emancipation. The dispute concerns a specific child. Its application: Muhammad said in the original al-Jami‘ al-Saghir: 'a child who has reason (sabi qad ‘aqal).' And in al-Jami‘ al-Kabir he placed the case for a child of twelve years. This indicates that the non-rational (ghayr al-‘aqil) is liable by consensus, because his being given authority is not considered, and his act is considered. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami‘ al-Saghir: 'a child who has reason,' and in al-Jami‘ al-Kabir he placed the case for a twelve-year-old boy. This indicates that the non-rational child is liable by consensus, because his authorization is not valid, and his act is considered.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (and also with al-Shafi‘i) regarding the liability of a child when he destroys property deposited with him. Two cases are considered: (1) killing a deposited slave, and (2) eating deposited food. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: in the first case, blood money (diyah) is wajib on the child's ‘āqilah (agnates); in the second case, the child is not liable. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi‘i, however, hold the child liable in both cases. The same difference applies to a slave under interdiction (mahjur ‘alayh): he is not immediately liable according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but will be after emancipation; Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi‘i hold immediate liability. This extends also to loans (iqrad) and loans for use (i‘arah). Finally, the passage clarifies that this dispute applies only to a child who has reason (sabi qad ‘aqal). For a non-rational child, there is consensus that he is liable, because his authorization is not considered and his destructive act is considered (i.e., he cannot be given property as a trust in a valid manner). The reference to al-Jami‘ al-Saghir and al-Jami‘ al-Kabir (Zahir al-Riwayah works) establishes the authority of the ruling.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadī‘ah): A deposit; property entrusted to another for safekeeping without compensation.
صبی (ṣabī): A child, specifically one who has not reached puberty; the dispute concerns a child with reason (gad ‘aqal).
عاقلہ (‘āqilah): The agnate group (tribe or family) liable for paying blood money (diyah) on behalf of a slayer.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property.
مجور علیہ (maḥjūr ‘alayh): A person under interdiction; here, a slave who is not free to manage property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling if a rational child (sabi qad 'aqal) eats food deposited with him?
A) The child is liable for the value of the food immediately.
B) The child is not liable for the food, but the 'āqilah pays if the child kills a deposited slave.
C) The child's father is liable for the food.
D) The child is liable after he attains puberty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds a discerning child liable for killing a deposited slave (diyah on 'āqilah) but not for eating deposited food, distinguishing between direct tort and consumption; this ruling is extended to slaves under interdiction.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Liability of a Child for Destroying a Deposit: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability of a child for destroying deposited property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on a child's liability for destroying a deposit and evaluate the proofs of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf/al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The owner forfeits inviolability when placing property in an incapable hand, so a discerning child is not liable for consuming deposited food.

This lesson unpacks a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is a discerning child liable when he consumes deposited food or kills a deposited slave? The positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad are pitted against those of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, with each side employing analogical reasoning (qiyas). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how differing assessments of capacity and inviolability (ismah) lead to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the two scenarios: (a) child kills a deposited slave, (b) child eats deposited food. Note that the slave case triggers diyah on the 'aqilah, while the food case concerns compensation.
The slave is treated as a living being with diyah, not merely property, which is a key distinction.
2
Identify the Disagreement
Clarify the positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the child is liable for the slave (diyah on 'aqilah) but not for the food. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold the child liable in both cases.
The same disagreement extends to a restricted slave destroying a deposit: liability immediate vs. deferred until emancipation.
3
Examine the Proofs
Analyze the proof of Abu Yusuf/al-Shafi'i: analogy to the slave case (where liability is admitted) and to a third party destroying the property in the child's hand. Then analyze the Hanafi proof: the property is not protected (ghayr ma'sum) because the owner placed it in an incapable hand, so the owner forfeited ismah.
The key concept is 'ismah (inviolability) and how the owner's action affects it.
4
Determine the Scope of the Dispute
Note that the disagreement is only about a discerning child (sabi 'aqil). For a non-discerning child, Muhammad's statements in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Jami' al-Kabir indicate consensus on liability. However, later Hanafi works show a split among mashayikh.
This nuance is critical: the later difference complicates the fatwa.
5
Extract the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Tarjih
The practical consequence: in a case of a discerning child eating deposited food, the mufta bihi in the school is generally the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (no liability), but caution is needed due to the later difference.
A mufti must be aware of both the classical and later positions.

قال وإذا أودع صبى عبدا فقتله فعلى عاقلته الدية وإن أودع طعاما فأكله لم يضمن وهذا عند إبى حنيفة ومــحــمد وقال أبويوسف والشافعي ضمن فى الوجهين

مجور علیہ غلام کے پاس مال ودیعت رکھا گیا اس نے ہلاک کر دیا تو ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں
وعلى هذا إذا أودع العبد المحجور عليه مالا فاستهلكه لا يؤاخذ بالضمان في الحال عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ويؤاخذ به بعد العتق وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي يؤاخذ به في الحال وعلى هذا الخلاف الإقراض والإعارة فى العبد والصبي
ترجمہ اور اسی قیاس پر جب کہ غلام مجور علیہ کے پاس کوئی مال ودیعت رکھا گیا ہو پس اس نے اس کو ہلاک کر دیا ہو تو طرفین کے نزدیک غلام فی الحال ضمان میں ماخوذ نہ ہوگا اور عشق کے بعد اس میں ماخوذ ہوگا اور ابو یوسف اور شافعی کے نزدیک اس سے فی الحال مواخذہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی خلاف پر قرض دینا اور عاریت دینا ہے غلام اور بچہ کو۔ تشریح اگر غلام مجور کے پاس کوئی مال امانت رکھا جس کو اس نے ہلاک کر دیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک غلام سے منمان کا مواخذہ بعد معتق ہو گا فی الحال نہ ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک فی الحال مواخذہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح اگر بچہ کو یا غلام مجو کوقرض دیا یا کوئی چیز عاربیت دی اور بچہ نے یا غلام نے اس کو ہلاک کر دیا تو منمان نہ ہوگا البتہ غلام سے بعد عتق مواخذہ ہوگا۔
اختلاف کسی بچہ کے بارے میں ہے اس کا مصداق
وقال محمد في أصل الجامع الصغير صبى قد عقل وفى الجامع الكبير وضع المسألة في صبى ابن اثنتى عشرة سنة وهذا يدل على أن غير العاقل يضمن بالاتفاق لأن التسليط غير معتبر وفعله معتب ترجمہ اور محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے "صبی قد عقل" اور جامع کبیر میں مسئلہ کو سال کے لڑکے کےبارے میں وضع کیا ہے اور یہ اس بات پر دال ہے کہ غیر عاقل بالا تفاق ضامن ہے اس لئے کہ تسلیط غیر معتبر ہے اور صبی غیر عاقل کا فعل معتبر ہے

تشریح یہاں سے مصنف یہ بیان فرمانا چاہتے ہیں کہ یہ اختلاف کسی بچہ کے بارے میں ہے عاقل کے یا غیر عاقل کے تو جامع صغیر اور جامع کبیر کے حوالہ سے ثابت کیا ہے کہ یہ اختلاف صبی عاقل کے بارے میں ہے ورنہ اگر بچہ غیر عاقل ہو تو بالا تفاق ضمان واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ بچہ کے غیر عاقل ہونے کی صورت میں اصل مالک کی طرف سے تسلیط تو پائی نہیں گئی اور بچہ کا فعل معتبر ہے تو اس کے فعل کے ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
تنبیہ - در مختار وغیرہ میں مسئلہ میں اس کے برعکس ہے یعنی صبی غیر عاقل پر بالا تفاق ضمان نہ ہو گا معلوم ہوا کہ اس باب میں ہمارے مشائخ کی دو جماعتیں ہیں۔ تنبیه - ۲ اصل الجامع الصغیر یہ مسئلہ جامع صغیر میں ہے مگر یہاں اصل کا اضافہ کیوں ہے؟ تو اس کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے ، علاوہ اس کے کہ یوں کہا جائے کہ یہ ناسخین کی غلطی ہے اور عین الہدایہ میں ہے فی الاصل اب کوئی اشکال نہیں رہتا مگر دیگر شروح میں ایسا نہیں ملا۔ امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کی دلیل
لهما أنه أتلف مالا متقوما معصوما حقا لمالكه فيجب عليه الضمان كما إذا كانت الوديعة عبدا وكما إذا أتلف غير الصبي في يد الصبي المودع
ترجمہ ابو یوسف اور شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے (بچہ نے ) مال متقوم تلف کیا ہے جو اپنے مالک کے حق کی وجہ سے معصوم ہے تو اس پر معلمان واجب ہو گا جیسے جبکہ ودیعت غلام ہوتا یا جیسے بچہ کا غیر مودَع بچہ کے قبضہ میں اس کو تلف کر دے۔ تشریح یہاں سے امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کی دلیل ہے کہ بچہ پر مال و طعام وغیرہ کا منمان کیوں واجب ہے؟ تو فرمایا کہ جیسے بچہ پر ودیعت کا ضمان بالاتفاق واجب ہے اسی طرح مال کا ضمان بھی واجب ہوگا اور اگر کوئی اور شخص بچہ کے پاس اس مال کو ہلاک کر دے تو مختلف پر ضمان واجب ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ اگر بچہ خود تلف کر دے تو اس پر بھی منعمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہ مال متقوم ہے اور حق مالک کی وجہ سے معصوم ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل
ولأبي حنيفة ومحمد أنه أتلف مالا غير معصوم فلايجب الضمان كما إذا أتلفه بإذنه ورضاه وهذا لأن العصمة تثبت حقا له وقد فوتها على نفسه حيث وضع المال فى يد مانعة فلا يبقى مستحقا للنظر إلا إذا أقام غيرة مقام نفسه في الحفظ ولا إقامة ههنا لأنه لا ولاية له على الصبي ولا للصبى على نفسه
ترجمہ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ نے مال غیر معصوم کو تلف کیا ہے تو ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ جیسے جبکہ وہ اس کو مالک کی اجازت اور اس کی رضا مندی سے تلف کرے اور یہ اس لئے کہ عصمت ما لک کا حق بن کر ثابت ہوتی ہے اور مالک نے اپنے نفس پر عصمت کو فوت کر دایا ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ اس نے مال کو ایسے ہاتھ میں رکھا جو کہ (ابداع و عاریت سے) روکنے والا ہے ( یعنی مجور علیہ ہے ) تو مالک شفقت کا مستحق باقی نہیں رہا مگر جب کہ مالک اپنے غیر کو اپنے قائم مقام کرے حفاظت میں اور یہاں اقامت نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مالک کو بچہ پر ولایت نہیں ہے اور نہ بچہ کو اپنے نفس پر ولایت ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume 15. Book of Blood Money. A slave is deposited with a child, the child kills him: the blood money is on the child's aqilah. Similarly, if food is deposited and the child eats it, is the child liable? Statements of jurists. All. He said: When a child is deposited with a slave and he kills him, the blood money is on his aqilah. If he is deposited with food and he eats it, he is not liable. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: he is liable in both cases. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: When a slave is deposited with a child, then the child kills him, the blood money is obligatory on the child's aqilah. If food is deposited with the child and he eats it, the child is not liable, according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said the child is liable in both cases. Explanation: If a slave is deposited with a child and the child kills him, the blood money is obligatory on the child's aqilah. If food is deposited as a trust and the child eats it, then according to both there is no liability, but according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i the child is liable. Regarding a restricted slave: If property is deposited with a restricted slave and he destroys it, is he liable? And on this, if a restricted slave is deposited with property and he consumes it, he is not held for liability immediately according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but is held after emancipation. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, he is held immediately. And on this same disagreement are lending and borrowing with respect to the slave and the child. Translation: And on this analogy, when a restricted slave is deposited with property and he destroys it, according to both, the slave is not immediately taken to task for liability, but will be taken after emancipation. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, he will be taken immediately. And on this same disagreement are giving a loan and giving something as a loan for use to a slave and a child. Explanation: If property is entrusted to a restricted slave and he destroys it, according to both, the slave will not be taken to task for liability until after emancipation, not immediately. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, he will be taken immediately. Similarly, if a loan is given to a child or a restricted slave, or something is given as a loan for use, and the child or slave destroys it, there is no liability, but the slave will be taken after emancipation. The disagreement concerns which child: its referent. Muhammad said in Asl al-Jami' al-Saghir: a child who has reached discernment. And in al-Jami' al-Kabir, he placed the issue regarding a child of twelve years. This indicates that the non-discerning child is liable by consensus because the authorization is not considered, and his action is considered. Translation: And Muhammad said in Jami' al-Saghir: 'a child who has discernment.' And in Jami' al-Kabir, he placed the issue regarding a child of twelve years. And this indicates that the non-discerning child is liable by consensus, because the authorization is not considered and the action of the non-discerning child is considered. Explanation: Here the author wants to explain that this disagreement concerns which child: discerning or non-discerning. So by reference to Jami' al-Saghir and Jami' al-Kabir, he establishes that this disagreement concerns the discerning child. Otherwise, if the child is non-discerning, then by consensus liability is obligatory, because in the case of the non-discerning child, the owner's authorization is not found, and the child's action is considered, so liability for his action is obligatory. Warning: In al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others, in this issue the opposite is found, i.e., the non-discerning child is by consensus not liable. So it appears that in this chapter our mashayikh are two groups. Second Warning: 'Asl al-Jami' al-Saghir' – this issue is in Jami' al-Saghir, so why is the addition 'Asl' here? There is no reason for it, except that one might say it is a copyist's error. And in 'Ayn al-Hidayah it is 'fi al-asl', so now no difficulty remains, but in other commentaries it is not found. The proof of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i: They argue that he destroyed valuable property that is protected as a right of its owner, so liability is obligatory upon him, just as if the deposit was a slave, and just as if someone other than the child destroyed it in the hand of the child-depositary. Translation: The proof of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i is that he (the child) destroyed valuable property that is protected due to the right of its owner, so liability is obligatory upon him, just as when the deposit was a slave, or just as if someone other than the child destroys it in the possession of the child-depositary. Explanation: Here is the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i for why the child is liable for property, food, etc. They said: Just as liability for the deposit is obligatory by consensus, similarly liability for property is obligatory. And if someone else destroys this property in the child's possession, the destroyer is liable. So it is known that if the child himself destroys it, he is also liable, because this property is valuable and protected due to the owner's right. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): They argue that he destroyed property that is not protected, so liability is not obligatory, just as if he destroyed it with his permission and consent. This is because protection is established as a right for him, and he has forfeited it upon himself by placing the property in a hand that prevents (from valid transaction). So he no longer deserves consideration unless he appoints someone else in his place for preservation, and there is no appointment here because he has no guardianship over the child, nor does the child have guardianship over himself. Translation: And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the child destroyed property that is not protected, so liability is not obligatory, just as if he destroyed it with the owner's permission and consent. This is because protection is established as a right for the owner, and the owner has forfeited it upon himself by placing the property in a hand that is preventing (from valid transaction, i.e., the restricted party), so he no longer deserves consideration unless he appoints another in his place for preservation. And there is no appointment here because the owner has no guardianship over the child, nor does the child have guardianship over himself.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a minor (sabi) for destroying a deposit (wadi'ah). The issue is whether a child who is entrusted with property (a slave or food) and then destroys it (kills the slave or eats the food) is liable for compensation. The Hanafi imams Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani distinguish between the two cases: if the child kills the deposited slave, the blood money (diyah) is due on his 'aqilah (the male relatives who pay blood money), but if he eats the food, he is not liable for the value. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, however, hold the child liable in both cases. The passage then extends the same dispute to a restricted slave (muhajjar 'alayh) who destroys a deposit, with the same split: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad defer liability until after emancipation, while Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i impose immediate liability. The text clarifies that the disagreement only concerns a discerning child (sabi 'aqil), as Muhammad specifies in al-Jami' al-Saghir a child who has reached discernment, and in al-Jami' al-Kabir a child of twelve years. For a non-discerning child, there is consensus that he is liable because his action is considered and there is no valid authorization from the owner. However, a warning (tanbih) notes that in later works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar, the opposite consensus is reported—that the non-discerning child is not liable—indicating a difference among the later Hanafi mashayikh. The proofs are then given: Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue by analogy to the slave case and to the case of a third party destroying property in the child's hand, concluding that the property is valuable and protected. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the property is not protected because the owner placed it in the hand of someone who is legally incapable of valid transaction (mamnū' al-tasarruf), so the owner forfeited the protection—unlike the slave case where the child had permission to hold the slave (but not to kill), and unlike a third party who is a capable destroyer. Thus, the child's lack of capacity to receive a valid deposit means the owner's act of depositing does not create inviolability for the food.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (‘āqilah): The male relatives of the killer (like the 'asabah) who are responsible for paying blood money (diyah) when a person commits unintentional homicide.
ودیعت (wadī‘ah): A contract of deposit where one person entrusts property to another for safekeeping without compensation.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for compensation; the obligation to make good a loss or destruction of property.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Property that has legal value and can be sold or compensated for in Islamic law.
معصوم (ma‘ṣūm): Protected, inviolable; property or life that cannot be lawfully violated without liability.
صبی (ṣabī): A child who has not reached puberty; in this context further divided into 'āqil (discerning) and ghayr 'āqil (non-discerning).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a discerning child (sabi 'aqil) eats food that was deposited with him, is he liable to pay compensation?
A) Yes, because the food is valuable and protected.
B) No, because the property is not considered protected (ma'sum) in the child's hand.
C) Only if the child was warned by the owner.
D) Only if the food was a luxury item.

Key Takeaway
The owner's act of depositing property with a legally incapable person forfeits its inviolability, so a discerning child is not liable for consuming deposited food, though he is liable for killing a deposited slave.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
12 min
Liability of an Intelligent Minor for Destroying a Deposit
Dispute on minor's liability for wadiah destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a minor's liability for destroying a wadiah and explain the rationale of inviolability ('ismah) used by each side.

Core Idea
If the owner entrusts property to an incompetent minor, the property loses its inviolability and the minor is not liable.

This passage presents a classic dispute within the Hanafi school and between Hanafis and Shafi'is. The question is: if an intelligent minor destroys property deposited with him, must he compensate the owner? The answer depends on whether the property retains its inviolability ('ismah) as a right of the owner or whether that inviolability is forfeited by the owner's own action. We will unpack the reasoning of both sides and see how the Hanafi school resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
Note that the dispute is about an intelligent minor (sabi 'aqil). For a non-intelligent minor, there is consensus that liability exists because there was no valid entrustment. Then identify the two camps: (1) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, who hold no liability; (2) Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, who hold liability.
The passage also notes a contrary view in later sources (al-Durr al-Mukhtar) regarding the non-intelligent minor, indicating two scholarly traditions among the Hanafi mashayikh.
2
Analyze the dalil of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i
They argue that the property is valuable (mutaqawwim) and inviolable (ma'sum) as a right of the owner. Therefore, destroying it triggers liability. They use analogies: (a) if the deposit were a slave, and (b) if a third party destroys the property in the minor's hand.
Their reasoning treats 'ismah as an inherent characteristic of valuable property once ownership is established.
3
Analyze the dalil of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They argue that the owner forfeited the property's inviolability by placing it with a person who cannot legally safeguard it. The owner's act of entrustment to an incompetent minor is analogous to giving permission to destroy. Hence, the property is not inviolable in relation to that minor.
Their view is that 'ismah is a relative right that the owner can lose by his own negligent act.
4
Examine the exceptions and refine the rule
The passage then gives three contrasting cases: (1) an adult or a ma'dhun slave depositor is liable because they have legal capacity; (2) if the deposit is a slave, the minor is liable because the slave's inviolability is based on his own potential freedom; (3) if a third party destroys the property, that third party is liable because inviolability is only dropped in relation to the minor.
These exceptions help delineate the precise scope of the rule: the loss of 'ismah is specific to the relationship between the owner and the minor depositary.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The passage, as part of al-Hidayah, presents the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad as the primary position. Although Abu Yusuf differs, the relied-upon fatwa is that an intelligent minor is not liable for destroying a wadiah.
This is a case of legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with the mufta bihi following the majority of the earlier masters.
