امام ابو يوسف اور امام شافعی کی دليل
لهما أنه أتلف مالا متقوما معصوما حقا لمالكه فيجب عليه الضمان كما إذا كانت الوديعة عبدا وكما إذا أتلف غير الصبي في يد الصبي المودع
ترجمہ ابو يوسف اور شافعی کی دليل يہ ہے کہ اس نے (بچہ نے ) مال متقوم تلف کيا ہے جو اپنے مالک کے حق کی وجہ سے معصوم ہے تو اس پر معلمان واجب ہو گا جيسے جبکہ وديعت غلام ہوتا يا جيسے بچہ کا غير مودَع بچہ کے قبضہ ميں اس کو تلف کر دے۔
تشريح يہاں سے امام ابو يوسف اور امام شافعی کی دليل ہے کہ بچہ پر مال و طعام وغيرہ کا منمان کيوں واجب ہے؟ تو فرمايا کہ جيسے بچہ پر وديعت کا ضمان بالاتفاق واجب ہے ايسے طرح مال کا ضمان بھي واجب ہوگا اور اگر کوئي اور شخص بچہ کے پاس اس مال کو ہلاک کر دے تو مختلف پر ضمان واجب ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ اگر بچہ خود تلف کر دے تو اس پر بھي منعمان واجب ہوگا کيونکہ يہ مال متقوم ہے اور حق مالک کی وجہ سے معصوم ہے۔
طرفين کی دليل
ولأبي حنيفة ومحمد أنه أتلف مالا غير معصوم فلايجب الضمان كما إذا أتلفه بإذنه ورضاه وهذا لأن العصمة تثبت حقا له وقد فوتها على نفسه حيث وضع المال فى يد مانعة فلا يبقى مستحقا للنظر إلا إذا أقام غيرة مقام نفسه في الحفظ ولا إقامة ههنا لأنه لا ولاية له على الصبي ولا للصبى على نفسه
ترجمہ اور طرفين کی دليل يہ ہے کہ بچہ نے مال غير معصوم کو تلف کيا ہے تو ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ جيسے جبکہ وہ اس کو مالک کی اجازت اور اس کی رضا مندی سے تلف کرے اور يہ اس لئے کہ عصمت ما لک کا حق بن کر ثابت ہوتي ہے اور مالک نے اپنے نفس پر عصمت کو فوت کر ديا ہے اس حيثيت سے کہ اس نے مال کو ايسے ہاتھ ميں رکھا جو کہ (ابداع و عاريت سے) روکنے والا ہے ( يعني مجور عليہ ہے ) تو مالک شفقت کا مستحق باقي نہيں رہا مگر جب کہ مالک اپنے غير کو اپنے قائم مقام کرے حفاظت ميں اور يہاں اقامت نہيں ہے اس لئے کہ مالک کو بچہ پر ولايت نہيں ہے اور نہ بچہ کو اپنے نفس پر ولايت ہے۔
تشريح يہ حضرات طرفين کی دليل ہے کہ طعام اور مال کے ہلاک کر دينے کی صورت ميں بچہ پر کيوں ضمان نہيں ہے؟ تو اس کی وجہ يہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمام اموال اپنے سب بندوں کے لئے پيدا فرمايے ہيں۔ اس لحاظ سے کسي مال ميں عصمت نہيں ہے بلکہ اس ميں سب کا اشتراک ہے ليکن اگر کسي ایک کو متعين اشياء کا مالک نہ بنا ديا جائے تو فساد کثير لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ ایک ہي چيز سے سب لوگ مشفع ہوں يہ تو ناممکن ہے اس لئے بر بناء ضرورت مالک کے حق ميں مال کو معصوم شمار کيا جاتا ہے۔ ليکن يہاں مالک نے يہ عصمت بھي ختم کر دي کيونکہ اس نے ايسے بچہ کے پاس مال وديعت رکھا ہے جو وديعت رکھنے کا اہل نہيں ہے تو اس نے خود اپنے مال کی عصمت کو ختم کيا ہے۔ لہذا جب اس مال کا غير معصوم ہونا ثابت ہو گيا تو بچہ پر ضمان بھي واجب نہ ہوگا اور نہ مالک اب مستحق شفقت رہا کيونکہ يہ تو ايسا ہو گيا جيسے بچہ نے اس کی اجازت ورضامندی سے اس کا مال ضائع کيا ہو۔ ہاں اگر حفاظت کے لئے کسي کو اپنا قائم مقام بنا ديتا اور وہ تعدی کر کے اس مال کو ہلاک کر ديتا تو ضمان واجب ہوتا مگر يہاں تو اس نے اپنا قائم مقام بنايا ہي نہيں اس لئے کہ مالک کو بچہ پر کوئي ولايت نہيں ہے اور نہ بچہ کو خود اپنے نفس پر ولايت حاصل ہے۔
مودع بالغ يا ماذون لہ غلام نے مال وديعت کو ہلاک کر ديا تو ضمان واجب ہے
بخلاف البالغ والمأذون له لأن لهما ولاية على أنفسهما وبخلاف ما إذا كانت الوديعة عبدا لأن عصمته لحقه إذ هو مبقى على أصل الحرية فى حق الدم وبخلاف ما إذا أتلفه غير الصبي في يد الصبي لأنه سقطت العصمة بالإضافة إلى الصبى الذى وضع فى يده المال دون غيره
ترجمہ بخلاف بالغ اور غلام ماذون لہ کے اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کو اپنے نفس پر ولايت حاصل ہے اور بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ وديعت غلام ہو اس لئے کہ غلام کی عصمت اپنے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اس لئے کہ غلام خون کے حق ميں اصل حريت پر برقرار ہے اور بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس کو غير صبي نے بچہ کے قبضہ ميں تلف کر ديا ہو اس لئے کہ عصمت ساقط ہو گئي اس بچہ کی طرف اضافت کرتے ہوئے جس کے ہاتھ ميں مال ہے نہ کہ اس کے غير کے حق ميں۔
تشريح. اگر مودع بالغ ہو لما ذون لہ غلام ہو اور مال وديعت يہ ہلاک کر ديں تو ان پر منمان واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کو اپنے نفس پرولایت حاصل ہے تو اقامت درست ہے اور عصمت باقي ہے لہذا ضمان واجب ہو گا۔
اور اگر وديعت ميں غلام رکھا ہوا ہوتو بچہ پر بھي ضمان ہوگا ( کمامز ) اس لئے کہ غلام کی عصمت حق مالک کی وجہ سے نہيں ہے بلکہ حق غلام کی وجہ سے ہے کيونکہ خون وغيرہ کے حق ميں غلام کو حريت کا درجہ ديد يا گيا ہے۔ اور اگر بچہ کے پاس کسي اور نے مال کو ضائع کر ديا ہو تو اس پر منمان واجب ہے۔ کيونکہ صورت مذکورہ ميں مال کی عصمت صرف بچہ
کے حق ميں ساقط ہے ورنہ اس کے غير کے حق ميں عصمت برقرار ہے لہذا اس غير پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
Book of Blood Money. Explanation: Here the author intends to state that this dispute is regarding a minor, whether he is intelligent or non-intelligent. It has been established through reference to al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Jami' al-Kabir that this dispute is concerning an intelligent minor. Otherwise, if the child is non-intelligent, then by consensus indemnity is obligatory, because in the case of a non-intelligent child, there is no delegation from the original owner, and the child's action is considered, so indemnity for his action is obligatory. Note: In al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others, the ruling in this issue is contrary to this, i.e., for a non-intelligent minor there is no indemnity by consensus. It is known that in this chapter our Mashayikh are of two groups. Note 2: 'Asl al-Jami' al-Saghir: This issue is in al-Jami' al-Saghir, but why is there the addition of 'asl' here? There is no reason for it, except that it may be said that it is a mistake of the copyists, and in 'Ayn al-Hidayah it is ['Fi al-Asl'] so no difficulty remains, but it is not found thus in other commentaries. The evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i: For them: that he destroyed property that is valuable and inviolable as a right of its owner, so indemnity is obligatory upon him, just as if the deposit were a slave, and just as if a non-minor destroyed it in the hand of the depositary minor. Translation: The evidence of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i is that the child destroyed valuable property that is inviolable due to the right of its owner, so indemnity is obligatory upon him, like when the deposit is a slave, or like if someone other than the minor destroys it while it is in the minor's possession. Explanation: Here begins the evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i: why is the indemnity for property, food, etc. obligatory on the child? It is stated that just as indemnity for the deposit is obligatory on the child by consensus, similarly indemnity for the property is obligatory. And if another person destroys this property while it is with the child, indemnity is obligatory on that other. Hence, it is known that if the child himself destroys it, indemnity is also obligatory on him, because this property is valuable and inviolable due to the right of the owner. The evidence of the two sides: And for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: that he destroyed property that is not inviolable, so indemnity is not obligatory, just as if he destroyed it with his permission and consent. And this because inviolability is established as a right for him, and he has forfeited it himself by placing the property in a hand that prevents (i.e., incapable of being an agent for deposit or loan), so he no longer deserves consideration unless he appoints another as his substitute in safeguarding. And there is no such substitution here, because he has no guardianship over the minor, nor does the minor have guardianship over himself. Translation: And the evidence of the two sides is that the child destroyed property that is not inviolable, so indemnity is not obligatory, just as if he destroyed it with the owner's permission and consent. And this is because inviolability is established as a right of the owner, and the owner has forfeited it regarding himself by placing the property in a hand that prevents (i.e., the contract is invalid), so the owner no longer deserves compassion unless he appoints another as his substitute in safeguarding. And there is no appointment here, because the owner has no guardianship over the child, nor does the child have guardianship over himself. Explanation: This is the evidence of the two sides: why is there no indemnity on the child in case of destruction of food and property? The reason is that Allah created all wealth for all His servants. From this perspective, there is no inviolability in any property; rather, there is common ownership. But if a specific person is not made the owner of specific items, great corruption would follow, because it is impossible for all people to enjoy the same thing simultaneously. Therefore, due to necessity, property is considered inviolable in favor of the owner. But here the owner has also ended this inviolability, because he placed the deposit with a child who is not qualified to hold a deposit. Thus, he himself ended the inviolability of his property. So when it is established that this property is non-inviolable, indemnity is not obligatory on the child, nor does the owner remain entitled to compassion, because it is as if the child destroyed his property with his permission and consent. However, if he had appointed someone else as his substitute for protection, and that person then transgressed and destroyed the property, then indemnity would be obligatory. But here he did not appoint any substitute, because the owner has no guardianship over the child, nor does the child have guardianship over himself. If a depositor who is an adult or a ma'dhun (permitted) slave destroys the deposited property, indemnity is obligatory. Contrary to the adult and the ma'dhun, because they have guardianship over themselves. And contrary to the case where the deposit is a slave, because the inviolability of a slave is due to his own right, since he is retained on original freedom with respect to blood. And contrary to the case where a non-minor destroys it in the hand of the minor, because inviolability is dropped only in relation to the minor in whose hand the property is placed, not in relation to others. Translation: Contrary to the adult and the ma'dhun slave, because these two have guardianship over themselves. And contrary to the case where the deposit is a slave, because the inviolability of the slave is due to his own right, since the slave is retained on original freedom with respect to blood matters. And contrary to the case where a non-minor destroys it in the hand of the minor, because inviolability is dropped only in relation to the minor in whose hand the property is placed, not in relation to others. Explanation: If the depositor is an adult or a ma'dhun slave, and they destroy the deposited property, indemnity is obligatory on them, because these two have guardianship over themselves, so the substitution is valid and inviolability remains; hence indemnity is obligatory. And if a slave is placed as a deposit, then the child is also liable (according to the correct view), because the inviolability of the slave is not due to the right of the owner but due to the right of the slave himself, since in matters of blood etc., the slave is given the status of freedom. And if someone other than the child destroys the property while it is with the child, indemnity is obligatory on that other. Because in the mentioned case, the inviolability of the property is dropped only in relation to the child; otherwise, inviolability remains in relation to others, so indemnity is obligatory on that other.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of a dispute within the Hanafi school and between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the liability (daman) of a minor (sabi) who destroys property deposited with him as a wadiah (trust). The passage begins by clarifying that the dispute concerns an intelligent minor (sabi aqil); for a non-intelligent minor, there is consensus that indemnity is obligatory because the owner never delegated possession to him and the child's actions are legally effective. A note is added that some later sources like al-Durr al-Mukhtar contradict this, indicating two opinions among the Hanafi mashayikh. The text then presents the evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i: they argue that the property is valuable (mutaqawwim) and inviolable (ma'sum) as a right of the owner, so destroying it necessitates damages. They draw an analogy to the case where the deposit is a slave (whose inviolability is inherent) or where a third party destroys the property in the minor's hand. In contrast, the evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the 'two sides') is that the property lost its inviolability because the owner himself placed it with someone incapable of proper custody. They argue that inviolability is a right of the owner that he forfeited by his own action. Thus, the minor is not liable just as if the owner had consented to the destruction. They refine this by explaining that inviolability is not inherent in property but requires a valid owner; here the owner's negligent act of giving property to a child who cannot legally accept it negates that inviolability. Finally, three exceptions are given: (1) If the depositor is an adult or a ma'dhun slave, they are liable because they have legal capacity (wilayah) over themselves. (2) If the deposited item is a slave, the minor is liable because the slave's inviolability is based on his own right (due to presumptive freedom in blood matters), not the owner's. (3) If a third party destroys the property while it is in the minor's hands, that third party is liable because inviolability is only dropped in relation to the minor, not others.

Key Terms
عصمة ('ismah): Inviolability of property; a legal protection that makes destruction compensable. In this passage, it is a right of the owner that can be forfeited.
وديعة (wadi'ah): A deposit; property entrusted to another for safekeeping without compensation.
ضمان (daman): Liability or indemnity for destruction of property; the obligation to compensate the owner.
صبي عاقل (sabi 'aqil): An intelligent minor who can understand the nature of the deposit but lacks full legal capacity.
اقامة (iqamah): Appointment of a substitute; the owner's act of deputizing another to safeguard the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's argument that a minor is not liable for destroying a deposit?
A) The minor lacked the intention to destroy.
B) The owner forfeited the property's inviolability by entrusting it to an incompetent minor.
C) The deposit was not valuable.
D) The minor had guardianship over himself.

Key Takeaway
An intelligent minor is not liable for destroying a wadiah because the owner forfeited the property's inviolability by entrusting it to someone incompetent, but exceptions apply for slaves, adults, and third-party destruction.

Minor's Non-Liability for Destroying Deposit
Explaining the rationale for minor's non-liability for deposit destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for why a minor is not liable for destroying a deposit and apply the concept of 'ismah to similar cases.

Core Idea
Owner forfeits property immunity by depositing with an incapable minor.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling: when a minor destroys property entrusted to him as a deposit, he is not liable. At first glance, this may seem unfair to the owner. However, the Hanafi school provides a rational proof based on the concept of 'ismah (immunity) and the owner's own role in losing it. We will walk through the reasoning step by step, clarifying the legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
What is the specific ruling? The minor is not liable (la daman) for destroying a deposit placed with him. Note the act: destruction of entrusted property.
This is a ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is a rational analogy (qiyas). The text argues that property originally lacks immunity; immunity is granted by necessity of ownership. The owner's act of depositing with an incapable person removes that immunity.
The proof is not a text but a logical deduction.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the analogy work? The original case: property not immune by default. The branch: property deposited with an incapable minor. The effective cause ('illa) is the loss of 'ismah due to the owner's choice.
The minor's lack of capacity is central.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold the minor liable. The Hanafi response is that the owner forfeited immunity, so no liability.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that the minor is not liable. The text emphasizes that the owner could have appointed a capable deputy, which would preserve immunity.
The ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Explanation: This is the proof of those who say that in the case of destroying food and wealth, why is a minor not liable? The reason is that Allah created all wealth for all His servants. From this perspective, no wealth has immunity (ismah); rather, there is common ownership in it. But if a specific person is not made owner of specific things, great corruption would follow because it is impossible for all people to benefit from one thing. Therefore, out of necessity, wealth is considered immune with respect to the owner. However, here the owner has ended this immunity because he placed the wealth as a deposit with a minor who is not eligible for deposit, so he himself ended the immunity of his wealth. Thus, when it is established that this wealth is not immune, the minor is not liable for compensation, nor is the owner worthy of compassion, because it is as if the minor destroyed his wealth with his permission and consent. Yes, if he had appointed someone as his deputy for protection and that person committed transgression and destroyed the wealth, then compensation would be obligatory. But here he did not appoint a deputy because the owner has no authority (wilayah) over the minor, nor does the minor have authority over himself.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the Hidayah, providing the rational proof for the ruling that a minor is not liable for destroying property entrusted to him as a deposit (wadi'ah). The commentator begins by stating that this is the proof of the two parties (likely the Hanafi school vs. opponents who might argue for liability). The reasoning is based on the concept of 'ismah (sanctity/immunity) of property. Originally, all wealth is not inherently immune; immunity is granted to owners out of necessity to prevent chaos. By placing the wealth with a minor who cannot properly safeguard it, the owner has voluntarily revoked that immunity. Therefore, the minor's act of destruction does not trigger liability. The commentator then distinguishes a hypothetical case where the owner appoints a capable guardian who then misappropriates the property – in that case, liability applies. Here, no such appointment occurred because the owner has no right to authority (wilayah) over the minor, and the minor has no authority over himself to accept such a role.

Key Terms
عصمت ('ismah): Immunity or sanctity of property that makes its destruction legally compensable.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A contract of deposit where one party entrusts property to another for safekeeping.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship over oneself or others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the minor lacks intention (qasd) required for liability.
B) Because the owner forfeited the property's 'ismah by placing it with an incapable person.
C) Because the minor is not required to repay until he reaches puberty.
D) Because the deposit contract is invalid from the start.

Key Takeaway
The minor is not liable because the owner's negligent choice removed the property's immunity ('ismah).

Three Exceptions to Minor's Non-Liability in Deposit
Listing three exceptions to the minor's non-liability for deposit destruction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three exceptions to the rule that a minor is not liable for destroying a deposit and explain the talil (rationale) for each.

Core Idea
Liability shifts when the depositor is an adult, the deposit is a slave, or a third party destroys it.

The general rule is that a minor is not liable for destroying a deposit in his care due to lack of legal capacity. However, the Hanafi school recognizes three exceptions rooted in the concepts of wilayah (authority) and ‘ismah (immunity). This passage details those exceptions and the reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule
Recall that a minor (sabi) is not liable for destroying a deposit because he lacks legal capacity (ahliyyah). The deposit's immunity ('ismah) is waived in relation to him.
2
First exception: Adult/authorized slave depositor
If the depositor himself is an adult or an authorized slave and he destroys the deposited property, he is liable. Reason: he has wilayah over himself, so his act is valid and the property retains its immunity relative to him.
The depositor is the owner, but his act of destruction is considered a breach of trust.
3
Second exception: Deposit is a slave
If the deposited item is a slave, the minor is liable for destroying it. Reason: the slave's 'ismah is for his own right (li-haqqihi), not derived from the owner. The slave is treated as free in matters of blood, so his immunity is not removed by the minor's incapacity.
This is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
4
Third exception: Third-party destruction
If a third party destroys the deposit while in the minor's possession, that third party is liable. Reason: the waiver of immunity is only in relation to the minor; it does not extend to others.
5
Apply the talil method
Each exception is justified by identifying a specific cause (sabab) that overrides the general rule. Understand how the legal reasoning (talil) differentiates these cases.
Talil is the process of providing a legal rationale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف البالغ والمأذون له لأن لهما ولاية على أنفسهما وبخلاف ما إذا كانت الوديعة عبدا لأن عصمته لحقه إذ هو مبقى على أصل الحرية فى حق الدم وبخلاف ما إذا أتلفه غير الصبي في يد الصبي لأنه سقطت العصمة بالإضافة إلى الصبى الذى وضع فى يده المال دون غيره ترجمہ بخلاف بالغ اور غلام ماذون لہ کے اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کو اپنے نفس پر ولایت حاصل ہے اور بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ ودیعت غلام ہو اس لئے کہ غلام کی عصمت اپنے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اس لئے کہ غلام خون کے حق میں اصل حریت پر برقرار ہے اور بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس کو غیر صبی نے بچہ کے قبضہ میں تلف کر دیا ہو اس لئے کہ عصمت ساقط ہو گئی اس بچہ کی طرف اضافت کرتے ہوئے جس کے ہاتھ میں مال ہے نہ کہ اس کے غیر کے حق میں۔ تشریح. اگر مودع بالغ ہو لما ذون لہ غلام ہو اور مال ودیعت یہ ہلاک کر دیں تو ان پر منمان واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کو اپنے نفس پرولایت حاصل ہے تو اقامت درست ہے اور عصمت باقی ہے لہذا ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ اور اگر ودیعت میں غلام رکھا ہوا ہوتو بچہ پر بھی ضمان ہوگا ( کمامز ) اس لئے کہ غلام کی عصمت حق مالک کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ حق غلام کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ خون وغیرہ کے حق میں غلام کو حریت کا درجہ دید یا گیا ہے۔ اور اگر بچہ کے پاس کسی اور نے مال کو ضائع کر دیا ہو تو اس پر منمان واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ صورت مذکورہ میں مال کی عصمت صرف بچہ کے حق میں ساقط ہے ورنہ اس کے غیر کے حق میں عصمت برقرار ہے لہذا اس غیر پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
Unlike the adult and the authorized slave, because they have authority over themselves; and unlike when the deposit is a slave, because his immunity is for his own right, as he is retained on original freedom with respect to blood; and unlike when someone other than the minor destroys it in the minor's hand, because immunity is dropped in relation to the minor in whose hand the property is placed, not in relation to others. Translation: Unlike the adult and the authorized slave, because both have authority over themselves; and unlike the case when the deposit is a slave, because the slave's immunity is for his own right, as the slave is retained on original freedom in matters of blood; and unlike the case when someone other than the minor destroys it in the minor's possession, because immunity is dropped in relation to the minor in whose hand the property is placed, not in relation to others. Explanation: If the depositor is an adult or an authorized slave and they destroy the deposited property, then compensation is obligatory for them because both have authority over themselves, so the contract is valid and immunity remains, hence compensation is due. And if a slave is deposited, then the minor is also liable for compensation because the slave's immunity is not due to the owner's right but due to the slave's own right, since the slave is given the status of freedom in matters of blood etc. And if someone else destroys the property in the minor's hand, then that person is liable for compensation because in the mentioned situation, the immunity of the property is dropped only in relation to the minor, but in relation to others, immunity remains, so that other person is liable.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary, explaining three exceptions to the rule that a minor is not liable for destroying a deposit. The first exception: if the depositor is an adult or an authorized slave, they have legal authority (wilayah) over themselves, so the deposit contract is valid and the property retains its immunity; thus, if they destroy it, they are liable. The second exception: if the deposited item is a slave, the minor becomes liable because the slave's immunity is inherent to the slave as a person, not derived from the owner. In Hanafi law, a slave is considered a legal person regarding bodily integrity (e.g., blood money), so his immunity is not compromised by the minor's incapacity. The third exception: if a third party (not the minor) destroys the property while it is in the minor's possession, the third party is liable. This is because the loss of immunity only applies in relation to the minor (due to the owner's negligence), but not to others. Thus, the general rule of liability for property destruction applies to the third party.

Key Terms
بالغ (baligh): An adult who has reached puberty and has full legal capacity.
مأذون له (ma'dhun lahu): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade.
عصمت لحقہ ('ismat li-haqqih): Immunity due to the person's own right, not the owner's.
اصل حریت (asl al-hurriyyah): Original freedom; the legal principle that freedom is the default status for humans except where slavery is proven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, why is a minor liable if the deposited item is a slave?
A) Because the slave has no immunity.
B) Because the slave's immunity is for his own right, not the owner's.
C) Because the owner loses immunity over a slave deposit.
D) Because the minor has authority over the slave.

Key Takeaway
The three exceptions demonstrate that liability depends on the legal status of the parties and the nature of the deposit, not solely on the minor's incapacity.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
6 min
Minor Liable for Destroying Non-Deposit Property
Stating that a minor is liable for property not deposited with him

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a minor's liability for destroying non-deposit property and explain the legal basis using the principle that a minor is accountable for his actions in financial matters.

Core Idea
A minor is liable for destroying others' property because liability in huquq al-'ibad attaches to the act, not intention.

In the previous lesson, we saw that a minor is not liable for destroying a deposit because the owner forfeited the property's protection. Now we encounter a different situation: when a minor destroys property that is not a deposit, he is fully liable. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that in financial torts affecting others' rights, the minor's actions trigger liability regardless of his capacity or intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states: 'If a minor destroys property (non-deposit), he is liable (daman).' So the ruling is that compensation is wajib upon the minor.
This is a ruling of tort liability, not worship.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites: 'because a minor is held accountable for his actions (yu'akhadh bi-af'alih).' This is a general legal principle applied here.
The dalil is aqli (rational) based on the nature of huquq al-'ibad.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The principle implies that liability is based on the act itself, not on the minor's capacity for valid intention. The commentary adds that soundness of intention is not considered in huquq al-'ibad.
This contrasts with acts of worship where intention is required.
4
Distinguish from sayings (aqwal)
The commentary clarifies that a minor is not held accountable for his sayings (such as contracts) because those require valid intention. But for destructive acts, liability is strict.
This shows the scope of the principle: it applies to af'al, not aqwal.
5
Evaluate the thamarah (practical effect)
The practical consequence is that a minor must pay compensation for any non-deposit property he destroys, regardless of whether he intended harm or was negligent.
This protects the rights of property owners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن استهلك مالا ضمن يريد به من غير إيداع لأن الصبي يؤاخذ بأفعاله وصحة القصد لا معتبر بها في حقوق العباد. والله أعلم بالصواب تشریح اگر بچہ نے مال ودیعت کے علاوہ کسی اور مال کو ہلاک کر دیا تو بچہ پر مضمان واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بچہ اپنے افعال میں ماخوذ ہوتا ہے اگر چہ وہ اپنے اقوال میں ماخوذ نہیں ہوتا۔ سوال بچہ کا قصد ہی صحیح نہیں ہے تو پھر یہ حکم کیوں؟ جواب حقوق العباد میں قصد وارادہ کی صحت غیر معتبر ہے۔ وَصَلَّى اللهُ تَعَالَى عَلى خَيْر خَلقِهِ مُحَمَّدٍ وَآلِهِ وَأَصْحَابِهِ أَجْمَعِيْن
He (Muhammad) said: And if a minor destroys property, he is liable – meaning without deposit, because a minor is held accountable for his actions, and the validity of intention is not considered in the rights of people. And Allah knows best. Explanation: If a minor destroys any property other than a deposit, then compensation is obligatory upon him, because a minor is held accountable for his actions, although he is not held accountable for his words. Question: The minor's intention is not valid, so why this ruling? Answer: In the rights of people, the validity of intention and will is not considered. And may Allah bless the best of His creation, Muhammad, and his family and all his companions.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage presents a separate ruling from the previous discussion. While a minor is not liable for destroying a deposit (due to the owner's forfeiture of 'ismah), he is liable for destroying any other property that is not a deposit. The principle is that a minor is accountable for his actions (af'al) in financial matters affecting the rights of people (huquq al-'ibad), even if his intentions are not legally valid. This is because liability in tort is based on the act itself, not on capacity or intent. The commentary contrasts this with the minor's lack of accountability for his sayings (aqwal), such as contracts or vows, which require valid intent. A question is posed: why hold the minor liable if his intention is not sound? The answer: in matters of others' rights, the soundness of intention is irrelevant; the act alone triggers liability.

Key Terms
استهلك (istahlaka): To destroy or consume property, making it disappear or unusable.
یواخذ (yu'akhadh): Held accountable or taken to task; legally responsible.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-'ibad): The rights of people (as opposed to rights of Allah). These are pecuniary rights where formalities may be relaxed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a minor liable for destroying someone's property that was not given as a deposit?
A) Because the minor has reached puberty.
B) Because the minor's intention is considered valid.
C) Because a minor is held accountable for his actions in financial matters affecting others' rights.
D) Because the property belongs to the minor.

Key Takeaway
A minor is liable for destroying non-deposit property because in financial torts affecting others' rights, the act alone triggers liability regardless of intent or capacity.
